Current Commentary

Reminiscing on the Tanggu Truce Anniversary: Remembering the Righteous Armies Fighting Against Japan 28

— Ting

According to various surveys, the number of times righteous armies appeared in Liaoning Province during the past year was as high as 6,298. The cumulative number of righteous army members was no less than 467,691. There were 134 leaders, not including the three provinces of Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol. In January and February of this year, the Japanese army mobilized to deal with the righteous armies in various places a total of 401 times, with 53,876 soldiers participating (excluding puppet troops). There were 182 righteous army leaders with 97,638 followers. In March, there were 4,734 recorded attacks by the righteous armies, with 277 leaders and 13,756 followers. Among the leaders, Wang Delin, Commander-in-Chief of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, Kong Xianrong, Deputy Commander, and Zhang Zhichao, Commander-in-Chief of the East China National Salvation Army, all have strong influence. The most active areas for the righteous armies are Fengcheng, Andong, Xiuyan, and Tonghua in Liaoning Province; Raohe, Hulin, Dongning, Ning'an, and Yilan (Sanxing) in Jilin Province; and Lindian, Anda, Hailun, Hulan, and Zhaodong in Heilongjiang Province; and Wujiazi, Sanjiazi, and Jialigou in Jehol Province. Their footprints can be found everywhere else.

With the Northeast fallen, the local righteous armies, compelled by righteous indignation, rose up in arms and fought bloody battles. Dressing their wounds, they continued to kill the enemy. The fact that our country's barely surviving national spirit and morale were able to be maintained and not decline is truly like the lingering light in the Lu Temple, which is all the more precious. The heroic and resolute anti-Japanese warriors stirred the ears and eyes of people within the Guannei (south of Shanhaiguan) and aroused strong sympathy. However, since the signing of the Tanggu Truce, rear support suddenly ceased. The righteous armies had no choice but to make a final struggle amidst hardship. On this anniversary of the signing of the Truce, reminiscing about the anti-Japanese warriors in the Black Mountains and White Waters, I truly have a feeling of unbearable regret.

The general public often underestimates the anti-Japanese movement of the righteous armies, thinking that the Japanese, with their sharp weapons, are like crushing dry weeds and destroying rotten wood when facing our loosely organized righteous armies. Therefore, they feel that the righteous armies are, at best, a minor irritation to the puppet regime and are not significant. In fact, this is just a common sense deduction and is not entirely true when considered in reality.

We do not need to be overly pessimistic about the current anti-Japanese movement of the righteous armies. What should be recognized is the following facts:

(1) The righteous armies all adopt guerrilla tactics. They break up into smaller units, and each small team operates independently. When the Japanese army chases a small number of soldiers, they surround and annihilate them. When there are many, they disperse and hide in the mountains. The Japanese and puppet troops are often exhausted and helpless.

(2) The Jidong Triangle Area (bounded by the Songhua River to the north, the Ussuri River to the south, and the Mudanjiang River to the west) has been a stronghold for the righteous armies since the September 18th Incident. The righteous armies there have now relied on natural defenses to dig trenches. On the one hand, they implement a system of land distribution based on population, with each household cultivating their own land and becoming self-sufficient. On the other hand, they select secluded places in the mountains and forests to train their troops and boost morale. This unit of the righteous army is the most organized and has the most strength. Many righteous armies from Liaoning, Heilongjiang, and Jehol provinces have come to join them after hearing about them. It is also said that they are preparing to complete an entire organization by mid-June of this year for long-term resistance against Japan. Recently, with the green gauze tents (tall sorghum stalks) rising and the clouds of war between Japan and Russia gradually thickening, Jidong is located between the borders of Japan and Russia. Once the international situation undergoes drastic changes, the righteous armies in that area will become a serious threat to the Japanese army in the Northeast. This can be asserted.

(3) Due to special circumstances, people in the Northeast have long had guns for self-defense. In order to prepare for war against Russia and eliminate the righteous armies, the Japanese ordered the puppet Manchukuo to confiscate civilian guns to prevent them from secretly communicating with the righteous armies. However, the people in various counties, feeling that it was difficult to hide and fearing that it would be difficult to revolt in the future, instead contacted each other and resisted. For example, more than 3,000 people from Chaoyang, Lingyuan, Jinxi, Xingcheng, and other counties in Jehol jointly launched an uprising and fought against the Japanese and puppet troops stationed there. People in Fujin and Hulin in Jidong took their guns into the mountains to join the anti-Japanese effort. Even those who did not go into the mountains were willing to voluntarily send their guns to the righteous armies rather than hand them over to the Japanese and puppet authorities. The situation in other counties, except for Liaoyang, Shenyang, Haicheng, and Panshan, which obeyed the order to hand over their guns, is also extremely chaotic. As of recently, the situation has become increasingly large-scale. The Japanese's actions have promoted the anti-Japanese united front between farmers and the righteous armies, which is worth noting.

(4) The troops of the puppet regime are forced by their living conditions and environment and are not willing to serve the enemy. Therefore, they often put on a show of force when attacking the righteous armies and are unwilling to exert themselves. They often mutiny and return to the right side when they encounter a suitable opportunity. Mutinies have been very common in recent months. There have been news of puppet troops revolting in Antu, Yingkou, Fusong, Changbai, Sanxing, and Jiaohe. The momentum of the righteous armies has greatly increased.

(5) Japan's invasion of Northeast China was intended to make the fertile land of the Northeast a place for its surplus population to live. However, since the implementation of immigration, it has repeatedly failed. The armed immigration in Jiamusi, Hunan, and other places in Jilin Province has been particularly difficult, and even the hard-earned businesses have felt thorny due to the attacks of the righteous armies. The difficulty of the Japanese immigration plan is due to the righteous armies.

All of the above may be sufficient to correct the public's understanding of the anti-Japanese movement of the righteous armies and not think that it has no far-reaching impact. Although the righteous armies are forced by their environment and cannot make grand plans to recover lost territory, they have stood on the front line of the anti-Japanese war for so many years and have been indomitable and brave. Their spirit of perseverance and determination can be a model for the people and deserves the highest respect. The signing of the Tanggu Truce is an ironclad fact in the past and need not be mentioned. Will we stand by and watch the anti-Japanese warriors on the front line and let them live and die on their own? Or will we wait for the opportunity to mature before providing them with strong support?

At the Disarmament Conference: A Head-on Collision Between Britain and France: Past Understandings Dissipated: Simon Directly Opposes Security Organizations: Advocates for the Rapid Establishment of a Disarmament Treaty: Barthou Attacks Germany's Restoration of Armaments: Expresses Unwillingness to Accommodate and Dig Its Own Grave 29

The General Commission held its third meeting today.

The British Foreign Secretary spoke first. (Geneva) After today's meeting of the General Disarmament Commission, British Foreign Secretary Simon spoke first, stating the importance of the Disarmament Conference and the entire system of cooperative efforts with direct words. Everyone knows that the British government is committed to resolving the deadlock, but has not yet reached a compromise on a new foundation. He is extremely dissatisfied with the policy of delaying and making empty talk. Changing the Disarmament Conference into a conference to discuss a security convention will not help. Now there must be practical progress. Regarding the question of whether Germany's plan to rearm can be the basis for an international agreement, he advocates for the immediate establishment of a draft treaty, incorporating the various clauses that have already been agreed upon and the necessary new concessions. He suggests three things: (1) chemical warfare, (2) budget, and (3) the establishment of a permanent disarmament commission. The British government feels that the method contained in the British memorandum of January 29 is more likely to produce an agreement than any specific proposal. The memorandum proposed by the representatives of Denmark, Spain, Norway, and Switzerland is in line with the one proposed by Britain. Simon concluded by saying that if the Disarmament Conference cannot adopt the suggestions contained in this memorandum or a similar approach, he does not believe that a disarmament treaty can be realized.

Barthou's Sharp Counter-Argument 30

French Foreign Minister Barthou spoke next, strongly refuting Simon's remarks and the British government's proposal, greatly straining the atmosphere of the meeting. He said that it is easier to achieve results by addressing the issue of security than by addressing the clauses contained in the British memorandum. France strictly abides by the 1925 Anglo-French agreement prohibiting the export of military supplies and implements of war (this statement is probably referring to the fact that Britain sold aircraft engines to Germany, and the British government claimed it was purely a commercial transaction). Given the difficulty of the situation, the time for euphemistic compliance or accommodation and compromise has passed. He knows that there are countries that have never feared aerial attacks but are now worried about the scourge of aerial warfare, but there are still other countries in the world threatened by land and naval forces. What he wants to know is, did Germany withdraw from the League of Nations, causing the agreement of last October to be impossible to implement? Can the Disarmament Conference allow itself to be manipulated by a country that insults the League of Nations itself? Britain has asked to build a path connecting France and Germany based on ideals that it believes France can gladly accept, but France is deeply concerned that there is a trap. He supports the French memorandum of April 17. Judging from Germany's military spending, it can be recognized that Germany has increased its war preparations, while France has reduced its military spending. The French memorandum has never closed the door to a general agreement and asks the Disarmament Conference to continue its work. France also supports its January 1st note, which has contributed all kinds of disarmament that the General Commission wants to have in the field of security.

French Foreign Minister Barthou's remarks have caused the Disarmament Conference to once again encounter the question of which is more urgent, disarmament or security. Barthou's remarks indirectly involve the actions of British Foreign Secretary Simon in past negotiations. The words are both satirical and unfriendly, arousing general criticism. According to the opinions of those in the audience, the French Foreign Minister's tone has destroyed the possibility of understanding between Britain and France. Seeing this development, Chairman Henderson announced a recess until Friday, so that the representatives would have the opportunity to consider the overall situation. (Reuters, 30th)

(Geneva) Although French Foreign Minister Barthou's speech was postponed for one day and was not announced at the opening, it still did not lose its spicy flavor. He made fierce attacks on Simon's mediation efforts and the position insisted upon by Germany. It was the most severe and explicit statement in French diplomacy since the first year after the European War. Barthou said that France's steadfast and unyielding attitude is truly admirable, because France still does not abandon its claim of last October 14 and will never allow a disarmed country to rearm. He recited the arguments made by representatives of various countries that day and said that they must not change their attitude because Germany withdrew from the League of Nations. However, France does not say that the door to the disarmament conference is closed because it has a note of April 17. Because the door to the disarmament conference is still wide open today. Barthou then made a detailed assessment of Germany's military preparations and budget, saying that the numbers were sufficient to prove that Germany had actually begun to increase its military preparations. As for security, Barthou said that he did not completely agree with Litvinov's proposal, but Litvinov's proposal had indicated a path for progress on the issue of security. (National Telegram, 30th)

Representatives of Various Countries Strive to Mend the Franco-British Rift: The General Commission Meets Three Times Today: Representatives of Small Countries Will Express Their Opinions 31

(Geneva) Representatives of various countries to the Disarmament Conference are very busy today trying to repair the wounds inflicted by French Foreign Minister Barthou's startling speech yesterday. The seriousness of the situation is well known to all, and the authorities' anxiety goes without saying. All parties are now working to break through this difficult situation. Representatives of small countries, such as Spain and Sweden, are very active. They held a meeting this afternoon to discuss ways to salvage the crisis and decided to use their memorandum of April 14 as a basis for making progress on practical issues. Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson is also trying to promote progress in the situation. Therefore, he met with British Foreign Secretary Simon, French Foreign Minister Barthou, and Swedish Foreign Minister Sandler today. It is heard that after the Polish Foreign Minister speaks at the General Commission meeting tomorrow, the representatives of various small countries will follow up and express their opinions. (Reuters, 31st)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Barthou's attacks on British Foreign Secretary Simon at yesterday's General Commission meeting is the only topic of conversation in Geneva today. Many representatives feel that they have now entered a stormy sea, and it is difficult to predict what will happen next. Because Barthou's remarks have been met with mixed praise and criticism. The Little Entente countries and those who support security first and disarmament second welcome it. However, even pro-French factions like Belgium regret that their remarks lack understanding. The Italians expressed their agreement upon hearing these attacks. One noteworthy point of the meetings in the past two days is that both Simon and Litvinov supported the organization of a permanent disarmament body. It is expected that this move will provide the General Disarmament Commission with a basis for continuing its work. According to news from Paris, the French newspapers believe that Barthou's criticism of Simon is a shocking development. Although critics generally believe that the British Foreign Secretary's remarks were disappointing, it is no wonder that Barthou made this criticism. However, they all consider this unexpected conflict between British and French policies to be strange. All newspapers hope that it will not have serious consequences. (Reuters, 31st)

But this kind of behavior should not surprise us, because representatives of Soviet Russia have no qualifications to condemn Germany, pointing to it as the center of world turmoil, because every child of three feet knows today that Moscow is the location of the microbe manufacturing plant. The whole world is still suffering from its infectious harm. Today, the scourge of communism has spread to countless countries, and Hitler has already given a considerable performance on how to prevent this scourge." (National Telegram, 30th)

The Börsen-Zeitung went on to comment on US representative Davis's speech, saying that the United States has felt the impact of European issues and is now paying special attention to it, which can be called satisfactory. A Speech by the Russian and French Foreign Ministers: Unanimous Sympathy from the French Press 34

(Paris) This morning, all the newspapers here commented on Foreign Minister Barthou's speech to the General Disarmament Commission yesterday. They unanimously believed that Barthou's speech represented the thinking of the majority of the French people. At a time when the danger of German rearmament is increasing daily, and when the insular mindset of Britain is still frequently expressed, the French people cannot help but feel a sense of antipathy. No one can more accurately represent this antipathy than Barthou in his speech yesterday. The press also believes that the greatest benefit of Barthou's speech is to once again establish the issue of security as the foundation of disarmament. (Le Journal) stated that people at the League of Nations unanimously approved of Barthou's speech, which shows that it deeply resonated with people. The wishes of France's loyal friends and allies, such as Poland and the Little Entente countries, were especially represented by Barthou. In his speech, Barthou greatly praised Mussolini's determination and his creative achievements, which made the Italians feel doubly happy. (Le Matin) summarized the spirit of Barthou's speech, roughly stating that Barthou first used extremely humble words to satirize the self-satisfaction of the British, then proceeded to use firm words to criticize the arrogance of Germany, and finally expressed regret at the passivity of the League of Nations. "Le Petit Parisien" stated that Barthou's speech was able to express the fear felt by the French people due to German rearmament. The Little Entente countries, the signatory countries of the Balkan Pact, and the Central European countries friendly to France all expressed satisfaction with this speech, which is clearly visible. "Le Petit Journal" stated that Barthou was able to express an unshakeable theory with a clear and firm attitude, and all those who agreed with Barthou's views felt heartfelt joy. "L'Echo de Paris" stated that people generally believed that British Foreign Secretary Simon's words seemed to advise people to value themselves with wisdom, but after Barthou's speech, this kind of mistaken thinking no longer exists. Barthou's speech is truly a major event in the history of the League of Nations. (Havas, 31st)

(Paris) The press greatly praised the speech given by Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov at the General Disarmament Commission yesterday. "Le Petit Parisien" stated, "In all of Litvinov's proposals, there is a part that can be put into practice. International assistance for peacebuilding is so sincere that it makes people feel doubly interested. We cannot but give credit to Moscow." "Le Petit Journal" stated that Litvinov's speech provided valuable support to France, because under the pressure of the political situation on the east bank of the Rhine, no one dares to regard security as a negligible issue. "L'Echo de Paris" believed that Litvinov's speech was issued after careful consultation between Paris, Moscow, Ankara, and the Little Entente countries. The newspaper stated, "Litvinov supports France's position on security and attacks the views of Britain and Italy. It can be seen that the empty talk and theories of the disarmament conference have ultimately led to failure over the past two years, and the responsibility should not be borne by France." "L'Intransigeant" stated that Litvinov's speech contained clever, good, and substantive suggestions. The newspaper's correspondent in Geneva commented on the matter, saying, "Litvinov's speech made a very deep impression. From now on, no country will be able to accuse France of improperly contacting Soviet Russia." (Havas, 30th)

Worried About Serious Consequences: The British Press Maintains a Cautious Stance 35

(London) Yesterday, the British and French foreign ministers delivered speeches in Geneva regarding the disarmament issue, and their opinions were quite divergent. The moderates and the Conservative Party in the British government both expressed regret and were very anxious about this situation. This can be seen in the tone of the newspapers. The newspapers mostly took a moderate tone regarding the disarmament proposals presented by French Foreign Minister Barthou. (Havas, 31st)

(London) Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov delivered a speech at the General Disarmament Commission in Geneva yesterday, advocating that the disarmament conference be changed into a permanent conference for safeguarding peace, to discuss various important issues to eliminate war. Judging from the initial criticisms issued by the British newspapers, it seems that only the remarks of the Liberal Party and Labour Party newspapers expressed sympathy for Litvinov's proposal. For example, the Liberal Party's organ newspaper, the News Chronicle, stated that Litvinov's proposal has considerable benefits and is worthy of careful study by the world, because the United States, Soviet Russia, and Japan do not need to join the League of Nations because of this, and can participate in the League of Nations' political work. Even Germany can more easily participate in the permanent conference proposed by Litvinov than in other meetings of the League of Nations. The Labour Party's Daily Herald also stated that the Russian Foreign Minister's words certainly have this kind of benefit. The newspaper had many criticisms of the Soviet Russian plan, because the Soviet Russian plan confirmed that a disarmament treaty could not be concluded. On the contrary, the Conservative Party's organ newspaper, the Daily Telegraph, held a different opinion, saying, "The Russian Foreign Minister wants to establish this kind of permanent conference outside the League of Nations. If this is not to say that Soviet Russia and other powers will be outside the League of Nations and display their management skills in the new conference, then we truly do not understand the reason." The Times stated that such a claim would allow Germany to return to Geneva and regain its former position, and faithfully adhere to its consistent view, saying that Hitler's proposal should be accepted by Geneva as a basis for reaching an agreement. (Havas, 30th)

League of Nations Political Conference Reopens Amidst the Ongoing Bolivian-Paraguayan War 36

(Geneva) The League of Nations Administrative Council is scheduled to meet at 10:00 this morning to summon representatives from the South American countries of Bolivia and Paraguay to discuss reports regarding the Chaco War. (Reuters, 31st)

Capital of Paraguay: This place is very happy to receive the good news today that the Paraguayan army defeated the Bolivian army at a fortress in the Chaco. According to the official announcement, the Paraguayan army annihilated the Bolivian Third Division, capturing many enemies and seizing many weapons. The enemy abandoned many corpses. The Bolivian and Paraguayan countries have been at war for a long time. Although the League of Nations is currently planning to stop the supply of arms to restrain the war, the effectiveness has not yet been seen. (Reuters, 31st)

Litvinov's Full Speech at the First Day of the General Committee: Suggesting that the Disarmament Conference be Changed into a League of Nations Peace Organization: Timely Assistance Should be Given to Threatened Countries 37

(Geneva) Yesterday, at the meeting of the General Committee of the Disarmament Conference, after speeches by Henderson and Davis, the Soviet People's Commissar for Foreign Affairs gave a speech. Litvinov's speech was based on the following facts: the issue of disarmament has no room for reconciliation due to the divergent opinions expressed at the conference, so it cannot be resolved. When Litvinov explained the main differences of opinion, he stated, "Two extremely different tendencies have been revealed from the beginning. One is represented by the Soviet delegation, and the other is actually advocated by other delegations. The Soviet delegation does not want to regard disarmament as an independent and self-sufficient issue, and is only satisfied with the purposes of budgeting, economics, propaganda, etc.

As Long as Disarmament Exists, War Cannot be Fundamentally Eliminated 38

We want to see disarmament as a true method to eliminate war. In the past and now, we believe that if armaments cannot be completely abolished, then war can never be truly eliminated. As long as armaments exist, peace can never be truly guaranteed. At the same time, we believe that only one kind of peace is possible, that is, the peace of disarmament, because armed peace is only a rest within the gaps between wars, which approves of war in principle and practice.

The Soviet Union's Disarmament Proposal: Unfortunately Opposed by Various Countries 39

The Soviet delegation once put forward a proposal for complete and universal disarmament. If this proposal had been accepted, then the divergent opinions on defensive weapons and offensive weapons, etc., at the conference would have disappeared, and from then on, the unfortunate political events that have occurred in various countries, as well as the deepening phenomena of nationalism, patriotism, and militarism, would have disappeared. At the same time, it would have an impact on the international economic situation. Therefore, I firmly believe that if the people of various countries (who previously had a greater influence on the policies of their respective governments) could similarly illuminate the development of international political life from the beginning, then they would never have allowed the conference to dare to despise the Soviet Union's proposal for complete disarmament in this way. Unfortunately, other delegations (I believe Turkey is an exception) opposed our proposal.

Up to now, we increasingly believe that once all countries resume their concept of relying on disarmament to avoid war through international methods, they must reflect on the Soviet Union's proposal for complete disarmament and carefully consider it, because there is no other guarantee of peace as long as the social and economic systems of non-Soviet countries exist today. When the Soviet delegation previously put forward this proposal, it did not take the form of a final ultimatum. On the contrary, the Soviet delegation expressed its willingness to cooperate with other delegations to create a system of partial reduction of armaments, and at the same time expressed that it would consider any kind and any form of armaments that could be applied to reduce.

To this day, there is no consistent opinion on the methods, principles, and regulations for reducing armaments. At the same time, there is no unified and established view on whether the so-called reduction should be applied to various forms of armaments (land, sea, and air forces). Although we do not list various complex opinions, we know that no problem has a concrete decision, and even a theoretical formula that can be agreed upon by the delegations is lacking."

National Policy is Strictly Enforced: Only Territorial Expansion is the Goal 40

Litvinov continued, "Political events did not wait for the end of the Geneva rhetoric. Within some countries, the government has changed, the ruling party has changed, and the consciousness of the party and the government has changed. The methods for solving international problems are no longer as they were in the past. Although all countries have accepted the Briand-Kellogg Pact, what we can witness is the strict enforcement of national policies. Its implementation is through the development of military actions in neighboring countries. Other countries, whose strength is insufficient to implement the same policies, are only afraid of not striving for the idea of ​​expanding with force and occupying foreign territories. The leaders of these countries have publicly announced their plans to occupy foreign territories, and the current issue is how to deal with these countries.

Negotiations Have Achieved Nothing: Revealing the Complete Failure of Disarmament 41

After summarizing the achievements of the conference over the past two years, we must publicly point out that the difficulties that were revealed at the beginning of the establishment of the conference have not weakened during this period. On the contrary, they have strengthened their tone and ultimately forced us into a desperate situation.)

Litvinov further discussed the informal negotiations held by some countries. As a result, no agreement was formed. Litvinov continued, "We have discerned the meaning of the statements made by certain two countries (neither of which are small countries, nor have they been harmed by their love of peace). They absolutely cannot agree to any method of reducing armaments. From this, they have demonstrated their firm spirit of aggression. These statements are sufficient to indicate the complete failure of the conference (in terms of its disarmament mission) and more than enough. Some delegations may suggest that the conference should be satisfied with the following half-step, such as re-establishing the prohibition of chemical warfare as an international obligation (which has already been passed), or re-establishing that armaments cannot be expanded further at the current level. However, in the current situation, who can believe that these obligations will actually be respected by all countries and that there can be practical control in practice? If we can be honest and open at this time and confess that international life, especially the political situation of some countries in recent years, has not allowed the conference to complete its direct task of drafting a disarmament treaty, would it not be more honest politically?"

Dissolution is Indeed the Right Conclusion: Seeking Ways to Guarantee Security 42

Litvinov continued, "The conference must be dissolved. This conclusion is followed up. If we deal with this issue purely from a formal and rigid point of view, that is, only keeping the name of the conference firmly in mind, then this conclusion is correct. However, the Soviet delegation continues to hold a broader view, believing that the conference has achieved its own purpose, which is none other than to realize a guarantee of peace through the method of disarmament. Therefore, the problem we are encountering is not only the problem of disarmament as a method, but also the problem of peace guarantee itself.

(Then a question arises, can the conference find other guarantees of peace for those countries that have no aggressive ideas, have no intention of war, and are targets of aggression once war breaks out, or at least limit and increase their security? We can ask, what kind of guarantee in the world can make the conference have greater consistency in its opinions on other issues than the previous issue of disarmament? And from this, make the new activities of the conference more effective and more successful? I dare to answer this question, in order to reduce armaments to a considerable extent, it is necessary to actually obtain the absolute agreement of all countries. The conference must do its best to make all countries comply with these programs, but even if some countries cannot agree, it must never prevent other countries from engaging in closer cooperation to implement these programs and enhance their own security.)

Supporting the Definition of Aggression: Sanction Steps Will Be Easier to Implement 43

Litvinov continued, "(The issue of security has been an old topic of this conference, and the conference has even established a special committee to deal with such issues.)" Litvinov then recounted the Soviet Union's proposal to define aggressive behavior, pointing out that "If those who support the definition of Soviet Union's aggressive behavior can continue to increase, then other proposals regarding security proposed at the conference can be more easily implemented. Similarly, new proposals can also be put forward, such as the proposal to impose sanctions on those who undermine peace or violate the Kellogg-Briand Pact. We can create various sanction methods without taking military steps, because the latter cannot be applied to all countries. On top of these somewhat universal conventions, we can add various regional conventions for mutual assistance, but this does not include military alliances or dividing countries into opposing camps, nor does it include steps to surround a certain country. The principle that all countries have equal rights without exception will never cause any doubts or hesitations under this kind of security step. Among us, some believe that the word (security) contradicts (disarmament), but in my humble opinion, there is no other way to find other expressions for the concept of (security) besides this. (If we can follow this path, then the time and energy spent at the conference will not be wasted, and we will not return empty-handed when we see the people who sent us here. The tendency of security and strength to consolidate can be understood by aggressive governments) or create such conditions, so that the issue of disarmament can be put back on the agenda, and there can be a better chance of success.)"

Renamed Peace Conference: The League of Nations Still Retains its Privileges 44

Litvinov further stated, "I absolutely do not want to limit the time and tasks of the conference. I respectfully suggest that the conference be changed into a permanent institution, which can provide the greatest possible concern for the guarantee of the security of all countries and the guarantee of world peace. In other words, my suggestion is to turn the conference into a permanent and regularly held peace conference to avoid the threat of war and its tragic consequences. The conference I am suggesting must create methods to consolidate security and complete it, issue timely signals for future war crises, and if countries feeling threatened make a request, they must approve it and provide appropriate assistance to them in a timely manner in terms of morality, economy, finance, and other aspects.)

Litvinov further stated that some opponents might say that the scope of what the League of Nations must engage in is not the same as what has been mentioned above. Litvinov then stated, "The tasks of the League of Nations are indeed too many, and it is also bound by the covenant. The paths to approach the League of Nations and obtain resolutions are greatly restricted by regulations. At the same time, the podium of the League of Nations can actually make it easier to step into a more free, and more attention is paid to the needs of the time. We let the conference be an organ of the League of Nations and be controlled by the League of Nations. We let the League of Nations maintain its original state, without making changes and completely maintaining its privileges. We want to establish another international organization outside the League of Nations and compete with the League of Nations? I have fully understood the difficulties. I will never make this suggestion. However, the convocation of the International Disarmament Conference has already shown the League of Nations' insufficient scope of activities for this great task of adding disarmament. My suggestion proposes a greater task, namely the permanent guarantee of peace. As far as I know, there is really no other way."

Enhancing Security in Eastern Europe: Russia's Policy Success is Worth Boasting 45

The Soviet government is quite proud of the security measures it has taken in recent years. These measures have had the most remarkable results in Eastern Europe, which is the region of greatest concern to the Soviet Union. Through the Convention Defining Aggression, the Non-Aggression Pact, and extending these conventions to the greatest possible extent, the Soviet Union has been able to strengthen mutual trust among the majority of its neighbors and increase their sense of security. The Soviet Union has created a new convention and declaration, that is, a convention and declaration that powerful countries can guarantee the independence of weak countries that are located between them or near them. I hope that this kind of convention and declaration will be widely adopted in the future.

Daring to Exert a Slight Effort to Strengthen Cooperation for World Peace 46

(The Soviet government's cause has not always been successful. It has not always received a response from the other party accepting its statement. However, even in these circumstances, the Soviet Union's proposal can still promote peace, because they can help point out where the actions that undermine peace can occur.) Litvinov concluded, "The Soviet government is willing to exert a slight effort to implement greater steps to guarantee world peace. This kind of cooperation with any international cause and any international organization will surely demonstrate the great moral strength of this ever-growing, strengthening, and powerful country with 170 million people. This powerful country has actually broken away from the past policy of military annexation, and its newborn sixteen years have shown a large amount of evidence of its love of peace." (TASS, 30th)

The Poison of Opium: The Four Northeastern Provinces are the Most Severely Affected: Hu Shih-tse Responds to the Accusations of the American Representative: Suggests Two Methods for the League of Nations to Implement: The Japanese Representative Remains Silent Throughout 48

(Geneva) At a meeting of the League of Nations Opium Advisory Committee today, American representative Fuller stated that opium and other dangerous drugs are greatly increasing in the three northeastern provinces, Rehe, Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu. According to Chinese government estimates, the total opium production in 1930 reached 12,000 tons. In 1933, China's opium production was seven times more than the total production in all other places in the world. Currently, opium smugglers are especially active in the three northeastern provinces and Rehe. Fuller also suggested that the League of Nations send an inspection committee to inspect various provinces in China and the three northeastern provinces and Rehe. (Central News Agency, 29th)

(Geneva) Chinese Minister to Switzerland Hu Shih-tse responded to the accusations of American representative Fowler at a resumed meeting of the Opium Advisory Committee today, saying that the Chinese situation has become more and more serious recently. It is unfortunate that he was unable to record the progress in the situation. However, China is determined to continue fighting and welcomes the technical assistance in the suggestion. It must be known that China suffers far more from foreign toxins secretly smuggled into its territory than other countries suffer from Chinese opium. He put forward two methods: (1) The great powers must not protect their people who are engaged in illegal trade; (2) Find ways to ban foreign ships engaged in illegal trade along the coast and rivers. (Reuters, 30th)

(Geneva) At the meeting of the Opium Advisory Committee, the representatives of various countries deeply acknowledged the seriousness of China's opium and other drug problems, and had the intention of making the Chinese government aware of the seriousness of the matter. They paid special attention to the secret manufacture of morphine and heroin in various parts of China. Spanish representative Quesada proposed that the Chinese government should quickly conclude the opium drug investigation that began a year ago, and report the results to the League of Nations as soon as possible. The motion stated that "The increasing seriousness of China's drug problem is sufficient to endanger the lives of the Chinese people, and to have a major impact on national economic development, political unity, and rural revitalization. At the same time, it will also seriously harm other countries." Also, American representative Fuller declared yesterday that the governments of various countries should take special measures to control certain chemicals specifically used for the manufacture of heroin. The quantity of these chemicals arriving in Shanghai is sufficient to manufacture up to one and a half tons of heroin per month. Quesada suggested that the same steps should also be taken to control the caffeine added to heroin pills. Our representative Hu Shih-tse put forward a motion that all foreigners who illegally manufacture or transport drugs in China should be deported back to their home countries and should not be allowed to come to China again in the future. Foreign ships traveling in the mainland that transport drugs should have their special permission to fly the foreign flag revoked. The motion is scheduled to be put to a vote tomorrow. It is expected that it can be passed without any major modifications. (Central News Agency, 30th)

(Geneva) People here familiar with the Chinese situation generally believe that the Chinese government's taking decisive steps cannot be delayed any longer. It has been repeatedly proposed here that the Chinese government should use customs and postal agencies to assist the authorities in preventing opium. Although the Opium Advisory Committee has repeatedly mentioned the situation of the poison spreading outside the Guan, and later our representative Hu Shih-tse also pointed out that the opium situation in the three northeastern provinces is serious, the Japanese representative has remained silent throughout and has not spoken. (Central News Agency, 31st)

US Fleet Arrives in New York; Roosevelt Leaves Capital for Review; First Time Since End of European War 49

(New York) The British fleet, which has been conducting exercises in the Pacific, Panama, and the Atlantic since April 9th, will arrive in the North River tomorrow to meet the seven million people of New York. President Roosevelt, as Commander-in-Chief of the Navy, will review the fleet. This is the first major review since the US fleet triumphantly returned from the Great War on Christmas 1918. Participating in tomorrow's review are 110 warships, 3,700 officers, and 44,000 soldiers. Millions of citizens will also watch from the shore. This event will showcase the glory of the American Navy, and thousands of soldiers, having served in the Pacific for many years, are now able to return to their hometowns. Many officers are also being promoted to new positions. (30th National Telegram)

(Washington) President Roosevelt left the capital today on a special train to New York to review the Navy. The flagship, the USS Indianapolis, is already docked in the Hudson River awaiting the President's arrival. Former Secretary of the Navy Daniels and current Secretary of the Navy Swanson are accompanying the President for the review. The President is scheduled to return to the capital on Monday morning. (30th National Telegram)

(New York) President Roosevelt boarded the flagship at midnight and departed before dawn to review the fleet. (30th National Telegram)

US Operations Commander Strongly Advocates Expanding the Navy 50

(New York) Admiral Standley today strongly advocated expanding the Navy to the limits allowed by treaties, and particularly emphasized the importance of frontline battleships. Standley is currently in New York arranging matters for the President's review of the Navy. Standley declared that if an enemy were to attack the United States by land, sea, and air, the enemy's first action would be to cross the ocean by ship. Therefore, the American fleet must be prepared to defend the nation at all times. A strong fleet is composed of various battleships and aircraft carriers, but battleships are the backbone of the fleet. Battleships are the fortress of maritime power, and only battleships can respond sensitively. Other ships or aircraft carriers do not have the ability to operate freely on the sea like battleships. Many old ships in the American fleet must be replaced with new ships to strengthen national defense. Naval experts and observers attach great importance to Standley's remarks, as the disarmament conference is uncertain, and Britain will also demand a reduction in the size of battleships at the future naval disarmament conference. Admiral Standley is currently the Commander of Naval Operations and is one of the world's leading naval experts, and may play an important role behind the scenes at the naval conference. The United States has few naval bases, and many are isolated from the mainland. Moreover, the United States has a very long coastline, and all its territories are isolated overseas, so there is a great need for large cruisers. However, Japan and Britain are eager to reduce the tonnage of large warships. (30th National Telegram)

Kaifeng City Holds Suburban Air Defense Drill 55

(Kaifeng) Kaifeng City held a large-scale suburban air defense drill on the morning of the 30th. The scenario assumed that an enemy aircraft, "Tianchu," was reported by the Lanfeng air defense observation post via telephone at 7:50 AM. Our fighter planes rose at 8:00 AM and engaged the enemy aircraft in combat for more than ten minutes. Assuming our air force was forced back, the enemy aircraft invaded the airspace and dropped bombs, poison gas, and incendiary bombs. The city's police, rescue teams, and firefighters were all pre-positioned in various locations and dispatched urgently to rescue and maintain order. Our anti-aircraft guns, anti-aircraft machine guns, and rifle squads fired into the air at the low-flying enemy aircraft, eventually damaging the enemy aircraft, which fled eastward. Our fighter planes tracked and pursued, and the drill concluded at 9:30 AM. Traffic in the city was stopped for two hours. (30th Central News Agency Telegram)

(Nanjing) Supervisor Shao Hongji impeached Kong Xiangrong three times for wasting public funds. The impeachment has been reviewed and approved and, together with the previous two cases, has been submitted to the Civil Service Disciplinary Committee for handling. (31st Special Telegram)

Syndicate's Planned Public Debt Issuance Transferred to the Ministry of Finance 64

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance previously needed large funds during the Fujian Incident and borrowed 44 million yuan from 16 banks in Shanghai, including the Central Bank of China, the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, using all of the Boxer Indemnity funds as collateral. A contract was signed on January 27, and Article 11 stipulated that the syndicate could issue securities worth 30 million yuan at one time. Now, the Ministry of Finance believes that the banks' funds are already tight during the silk and tea market season, but this year, due to the decline in international trade, the demand for funds is not high, and the funds are still very loose. Therefore, there is no need to issue this public debt. It has been agreed with the syndicate to transfer the public debt planned to be issued by the banks to the Ministry of Finance for issuance. The Ministry of Finance believes that the Shanghai banking community has unanimously approved the issuance by the Ministry of Finance. However, the Ministry of Finance will acknowledge and subsidize the various losses incurred by the syndicate during the preparation. The securities will be issued within this month, and the issued securities will be sold to the syndicate, and the banks can still use them as cash collateral or for trading. (31st Special Telegram)

Legislative Yuan Reviews Revised Cigarette Tax Bill 65

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held a review meeting on the revised cigarette consolidated tax rate bill on the morning of the 31st. Representatives from the Taxation Department of the Ministry of Finance went to present their views. The Legislative Yuan stated that the current two-tiered cigarette consolidated tax rate is too simple. Goods of different prices are taxed at the same rate, causing domestic cigarette factories to be oppressed by foreign merchants. It would be best to classify domestic cigarettes and assess taxes based on their grade, in addition to the factory tax. Otherwise, the intention to encourage domestic goods should be specially indicated in the ad valorem or specific tax. Wei Tingsheng's investigation results were also presented for discussion. The Ministry of Finance representatives stated that too many grades would be difficult, but they agreed to carefully consider revising the factory tax to encourage and protect domestic products. No final decision was made at the time, and further discussions will be held next week. (31st Special Telegram)

Rumor that Japan Plans to Ask China to Establish Police Stations in Fuzhou and Xiamen 66

(Nanjing) According to a news report from an unspecified media outlet, in addition to discussing and resolving the North China and economic issues during his visit, the Japanese Ambassador Arima Akio will also take the opportunity to request that China allow Japan to establish a number of Japanese police stations in Fuzhou and Xiamen, on the grounds that there are many Taiwanese residents in the Fuzhou and Xiamen areas, in order to facilitate management. (31st Special Telegram)

National Government Issues Order Prohibiting Foreign Loans 67

(Nanjing) The National Government approved the letter from the Central Political Council to various agencies, stating that no foreign loans should be borrowed without authorization in any name. A special order was issued on the 29th to all directly affiliated agencies, instructing their subordinates to comply, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was instructed to notify various embassies for their information. (30th Central News Agency Telegram)

Ministry of Communications Negotiates Loan from British Boxer Indemnity Funds to Finance Long-Distance Telephone Project in Nine Provinces 70

(Nanjing) In order to implement the long-distance telephone project in nine provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Henan, Hebei, Shandong, and Shanxi, the Ministry of Communications has applied to the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Committee for a loan of £200,000 from the Huai River guiding Boxer Indemnity funds for the purchase of materials. The Boxer Indemnity Committee has approved the loan, and the loan contract will be signed soon, stipulating that the principal and interest will be repaid in installments starting one year after the completion of the nine-province long-distance telephone project. (31st Special Telegram)

Central Government Stipulates Procedures for Party Members to Transfer Residences 71

(Nanjing) The Central Executive Committee has ordered the party headquarters of all provinces and cities that party members who move from place A to place B should apply for leave from place A if they are temporarily residing in place B. Otherwise, the sub-branch in place A can punish them according to regulations. If they are permanently residing in place B for more than two months and have not completed the transfer registration procedures, the local party headquarters can inquire about it. If they still do not comply, they should be handled in accordance with the disciplinary regulations for unjustified absence. (31st Special Telegram)

Sino-Japanese Communication Will Not Hold Any Ceremonies 72

(Nanjing) Because Sino-Japanese communication has often been sent via Japanese submarine cables in the past, which is time-consuming and uneconomical, the Ministry of Communications has sought the consent of the Japanese side to discuss establishing a Sino-Japanese radio station for direct communication. It is scheduled to officially begin communication at 8:00 AM on the 1st at the Shanghai International Radio Station and the Tokyo Radio Station. Minister Zhu Jiahua believes that direct Sino-Japanese communication is a normal matter and there is no need to hold any ceremonies. He has telegraphed Wen Yuqing to inform him of this decision. (31st Special Telegram)

Reorganization of the Executive Yuan; Central Antiquities Preservation Committee 73

(Nanjing) After the Palace Museum case, the Executive Yuan decided to reorganize the Central Antiquities Preservation Committee. The number of committee members is set at 15. Lu Xirong, director of the Department of Rites and Customs of the Ministry of Interior, and Zhang Jiong, director of the Department of Social Education of the Ministry of Education, are ex officio members. For the expert members, the Executive Yuan decided at its meeting on Tuesday to appoint Ye Gongchuo and five others as members of the Preservation Committee. There are still several experts to be announced soon. The Antiquities Preservation Committee was previously established by the government in 1932, and now it is being reorganized due to factual needs. Its task is to identify antiquities and supervise their preservation, which does not conflict with the functions of the Palace Museum. (31st Special Telegram)

Reuters Special Business Telegram, May 31 87

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price: The London gold price today was 136 shillings and 11.5 pence, down 1 pence from yesterday.

London Silver Bar: The London silver market remained unchanged today. Spot prices are still quoted at 19 5625 pence, and futures are at 19 625 pence. US buying and Indian selling occurred in the morning, with minor transactions. New York Silver Bar: The silver market opened steadily, with no pressure from sellers. However, sentiment was mixed, and traders are closely watching developments in Washington. Opening prices were approximately 30 to 40 pounds higher than London. Therefore, today's opening prices for deferred contracts in this silver market are generally lower than Tuesday's closing prices by 2 to 7 pounds, except for December, which is 20 pounds higher.

Bombay Silver Bar: The Bombay silver market closed steady today. The spot price was 54 rupees and 6 annas, up 5 annas. Futures also rose 5 annas.

Exchange Rates 88

British-American: The US dollar rose slightly this morning due to a slight selling of francs by foreign exchange managers. The British-American exchange rate opened at $5.07125, up 125 from yesterday's close. It then rose 5625 to $5.076875, before falling 125 to $5.075625. There were no further changes. Also, one US dollar equals 3 shillings and 11.296 pence in British gold.

British-French: The opening was 77 francs, up 4 pounds from yesterday. It briefly rose 9 pounds to 77.09 francs, before falling back 6 pounds to 77.03 francs. The price remained unchanged until the time of the telegram.

American-British: The American-British exchange rate opened at $5.07375, down 375 from Tuesday's close. It then fell another 25 to $5.07125.

American-French: The New York exchange rate for French francs opened at 6.59.00.

British Wheat: Liverpool wheat market, July futures at 4 shillings and 8.125 pence, up 125.

Valiant Sacrifice of Righteous Army in Jilin 109

Request to Demarcate Thirteen Counties for Defense by the Righteous Army

Japanese and Puppets Fear Heightened Popular Sentiment, Agree to Three Counties

Harbin dispatch: The counties near Yilan, Jilin, were previously the scene of popular uprisings sparked by the Japanese army's oppression in confiscating firearms and seizing land. Xie Wendong's suicide of his entire family to rally the righteous army marked the beginning. His call to action resonated widely, leading to even more tragic and heroic acts. Over ten high school graduates from Harbin, before resolving to sacrifice themselves in resistance against Japan, first asked their parents to find a way to survive on their own. Dressed in mourning clothes and hats, they knelt before their parents, lamenting the unbearable oppression of the violent Japanese and seeking to avoid mutual destruction. If elderly individuals still clung to their remaining years and were unwilling to take their own lives, they agreed on a cruel method of exchanging roles to kill each other's parents. The Zhang family members killed the Wang family's parents, while the Wang family members killed the Zhang family's parents, either with poison or gunfire, in various ways. After resolving matters with each other, they then killed their wives and children before swearing an oath to the heavens to fight the Japanese army to the death. No fewer than ten such tragedies occurred. As a result, their solidarity became stronger, gathering over 30,000 people. The Japanese and puppet forces mobilized their army, navy, and air force in joint operations, repeatedly pursuing and attacking them without success and suffering great losses. Now, the Japanese and puppets, recognizing that popular sentiment cannot be violated, have changed their tactics. They instigated Wang, a staff officer in Yu Nichen's conscription department, to go and persuade the righteous army to surrender. The righteous army, aware of the Japanese and puppets' plot, made extremely harsh demands. They demanded that thirteen counties in eastern Jilin, including Yilan, Huachuan, and Boli, be designated as the sphere of influence of the righteous army, declaring it as Chinese territory. Furthermore, Japanese and puppet officials and troops would not be allowed to operate within these twelve counties. The Japanese and puppet side only agreed to designate Yilan, Huachuan, and Boli counties as the sphere of influence of the righteous army. It is reported that the two sides are still continuing negotiations. (Northeast News Agency)

Li Du's Telegram to Gu Weijun 110

Painful Account of the Devastation Suffered by the People of Yilan

Please Report to the League of Nations to Appeal on Behalf of the People

General Li Du, in a telegram to Gu Shaochuan on May 19th, stated: "To Honorable Mr. Gu Shaochuan, As the League of Nations convenes to discuss the Far East issue, you are striving to defend our nation's sovereignty and uphold justice for humanity on the international stage. I look up to your brilliance with profound admiration. Recently, the Japanese have intensified their brutality in the Northeast, such as (1) forcibly conscripting young men into the army, (2) confiscating the people's self-defense weapons, (3) revoking the people's land deeds, (4) massacring innocent youths, and (5) publicly selling opium. Intellectuals with any sense of national identity are not spared. The cruel policies of national subjugation and extermination have reached their extreme. Yet, they continue to deceive the international community in various ways in an attempt to mislead them. It is reported that Zhang Yuanliang, a representative of the people of Lin Yilan County, disguised himself and came to Shanghai to report that at 11:00 AM on March 10th, the Japanese implemented armed immigration in the Tulong Mountain area, 100 li southeast of the county. Many Koreans, accompanied by Japanese soldiers, forced local farmers to abandon their possessions, surrender their firearms and land deeds, and relocate immediately. A man named Luan, driven to despair, shot and killed his entire family of over twenty women and children and contacted 15,000 fellow villagers, who, in their rage, killed the Japanese military officer Iizuka and over 100 Japanese soldiers. The Japanese side dispatched a large number of troops to attack and used 45 aircraft to bomb the villages, intending to wipe them out. At the same time, similar incidents occurred in the neighboring counties of Boli and Huachuan. The leader of the uprising is Xie Dongshan, who has now made contact with Luan. The three counties have tens of thousands of armed farmers, holding strategic locations and confronting the Japanese army. However, their equipment is crude and outdated, and they fear that they will not be able to sustain the resistance in the end. If no appropriate solution is found, our compatriots in the Northeast will face annihilation. I implore you to publicize this tragic situation to the assembly so that the international community can understand the truth and the Japanese schemes will be exposed. I am choking with emotion as I write this telegram. Please take note. Respectfully, Li Du." (China United News Agency)

Japanese Consulate in Xiamen Conducts Census of Registered Residents Intended to Move Taiwanese People into Fujian 111

Xiamen Correspondence: The Japanese residents, Taiwanese, originally migrated from Southern Fujian, Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, etc. Therefore, the four million Taiwanese people now all speak the Xiamen dialect, and their customs are completely the same as those of Southern Fujian. For this reason, the Taiwanese who reside in Southern Fujian are the majority, especially with Xiamen as the center. The Japanese recently proposed to move Taiwanese people into Fujian, and their goal is in Southern Fujian and Xiamen City. The number of Taiwanese people in Xiamen has been gradually increasing recently. According to news from the Japanese consulate, there are more than 30,000 people. However, many came to Fujian without permits and have not registered with the Japanese consulate. The Japanese consulate recently ordered the Xiamen Taiwanese Association to assign Taiwanese people throughout the Xiamen Island, according to the regional cities of each Xiamen security self-government association, and divide into twenty-two districts to form Taiwanese security committees in each district and appoint security committee members in each district to manage the Taiwanese people within the district under the command of the Japanese Consul’s Office police chief, forming a strict and systematic organization. The first step is to investigate the household registration and personnel changes of Taiwanese people in each district. However, Taiwanese people who registered with the Japanese consulate upon arriving in Xiamen according to regulations only reached a little over 10,000 people as of recently, and there are still over 10,000 people who have not registered. The Japanese Consul recently actively organized Taiwanese people in Xiamen by issuing a letter from the Police Chief to the Taiwan Association, informing Taiwanese people residing in Xiamen to go to the Consulate to register and report within one month. The Taiwan Association and the Police Chief jointly issued a public announcement a few days ago, urging Taiwanese residing in Xiamen to go to the office to register. (May 28th)

Zhu, Hu, and He Arrive in Jiangxi 112

Nanchang Correspondence: Zhu Shaoliang, Chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government and concurrently Director of Pacification for Gansu, Ningxia, and Qinghai Provinces, flew from Lanzhou to Jiangxi to meet with Chiang on May 24. He stayed in Xi'an on the same day and flew to Hankou on the 25th. On the morning of the 28th, at around 9 AM, he flew from Hankou to Jiangxi and arrived in Nanchang at 11 AM on the same day. The Reception Section of the General Affairs Office of the Headquarters sent people to the airport to welcome him. Zhu and his entourage stayed at the Great Hotel and reported to the Reception Section of the General Affairs Office of the Headquarters. Chiang is scheduled to meet with him on the 29th. It is said that Zhu's mission in Jiangxi is to report on the administrative situation in Gansu, the current military situation in the three provinces, the process of suppressing Sun Dianying, and the defense situation after the demobilization of the units that suppressed Sun. The following points will be discussed: (1) Request the central government to allocate funds to relieve the disaster victims in the Ningxia war zone and provide pacification. (2) Develop the Northwest, such as completing the Shaanxi-Gansu highway, constructing water conservancy projects, improving animal husbandry, and preventing and controlling veterinary diseases. Because Song Ziwen previously inspected the Northwest and established a complete plan, Zhu's arrival is to urge its early implementation. (3) Consolidate the construction and border defense of the Northwest. After obtaining substantial results, he will return to Gansu immediately.

Hu Zongnan also arrived in Jiangxi yesterday to meet with Chiang, reporting on the demobilization process after suppressing Sun, the defense of his units, and the situation of replenishment and training. Chiang praised him greatly.

He Jian, Chairman of Hunan and concurrently Commander-in-Chief of the Western Route of the Jiangxi-Guangdong-Fujian-Hunan-Hubei Bandit Suppression Army, arrived in the province on the train from Changsha via Hankou and the Nanchang-Xunpu Road on May 28. At around 2 PM in the afternoon, the train arrived at the Niuxing Station. Director Cai and Section Chief Wang of the Headquarters went to the station to welcome him. He stayed at the Garden Hotel. According to He, the mission of his visit is to report to Chairman Chiang on the bandit suppression situation on the border of Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan, and to request instructions on follow-up measures. He also said that the western route defense area is vast, covering 43 counties (from Suichuan along the west of the Gan River and east of Hunan to Chongtong in southern Hubei). The Red bandits have always been suppressed in this area and flee to that area, appearing and disappearing unpredictably. Because the military strength is limited, it is difficult to deploy forces to the fullest extent, so encirclement and suppression often encounter difficulties. Currently, the bandits in the western route defense area have been defeated and broken into smaller groups. The larger groups are still two in number: Xiao Ke and Cai Huiwen between Anfu, Yongxin, and Lianhua; and Gao Yongsheng between Xiushui, Tonggu, and Chongtong on the border of Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan. It is feared that it will take some effort to suppress them. As for the scattered bandits in the four villages of other counties, political and military forces must arrive together to be effective. The Jiangxi-Hunan border highway has either been completed or is under active construction. Although the Jiangxi militia cannot be compared with Hunan at this time, the Hunan militia has spent five or six years to organize. Therefore, the training of the militia is even more difficult than the army. When asked about the rumors that the main force of Zhu and Mao on the border of Jiangxi and Fujian was surrounded and would cross the Gan River from Xingguo and Wan'an to flee to the border of Hunan, He replied that based on the current military situation of bandit suppression, he could guarantee that the Red bandits would not take this move. (May 28th)

Guangxi Province Prohibits Export of Cash Confiscate All Amounts Exceeding 50 Yuan 113

Guangzhou Correspondence: A run on paper currency suddenly occurred in Guangxi Province a month ago and has not been fully resolved yet. Recently, Wuzhou City has banned the export of cash to maintain finance. The garrison army stationed in Wuzhou convened a meeting of various agencies yesterday to discuss maintenance measures. Everyone believed that there were recently criminals in Wuzhou City making rumors (rumors that Bai Chongxi was assassinated in Guangxi) in an attempt to disrupt finance, and even some unscrupulous merchants went to various places to collect Guilin paper currency and take it to the bank for redemption to seek profit, resulting in another run on the bank. If this continues and is not suppressed, not only will finance be disrupted, but it will also affect security. They immediately agreed on suppression measures: the export of cash in Wuzhou is limited to 50 yuan, and the 19th Division Headquarters stationed in Wuzhou will issue inspection certificates and send inspectors to the east, west, north, and south and other places such as Xiaguan Jiangjun Bridge to conduct inspections. If anyone carries cash exceeding the prescribed 50 yuan, it will be confiscated in full. (May 25th)

Shen Jinyun, the captain of the Criminal Investigation Team of the Public Security Bureau, interceded with Hu, who refused, and the case was transferred to the court. Yesterday, a man named Shi Ruishou, dressed in opium attire, was carrying more than 190 taels of opium. He was traveling by car and saw a police patrolman on the road at Pingqiao. He quickly hid the package behind his seat. The police officer, Xu Guoliang, found his behavior suspicious and ordered a search. Meningitis Patient on the Brink of Death 115

Wu Meiting, an apprentice at the Songcheng Zhou Pharmacy, suddenly contracted meningitis a few days ago. The condition was very serious, and he was rushed to Songjiang Hospital for treatment. Director Zhang Shaoxiu immediately used a needle to draw and test the spinal cord. The marrow had turned green, and it seemed to have festered. There was little hope of saving him. However, Director Zhang still tried to inject medicine. The patient fell into a coma yesterday and was unconscious. A few days ago, the county government reported to Director Zhang that meningitis was about to disappear, but epidemic prevention should be carried out in advance. Wujiang Money Industry Association Organizes Reserve Bank 119

The members of the Wujiang County Money Industry Association held a standing committee meeting on May 28th in Tongli. They saw that the rural economy was collapsing, industry and commerce were declining, and the impact on the interior was even greater. Money shops are the general hub of finance, and their responsibility is to regulate and adjust, which is their unavoidable duty. However, in this unfavorable situation, money shops themselves must also help each other to consolidate the financial foundation in order to have sufficient power to regulate the society. Therefore, at the meeting, it was resolved to organize a reserve bank for members of the same industry. It is said that the site of the bank will be temporarily attached to the Changfeng Zhuang, and Lu Yousheng, the manager of Jinfeng, was elected as the director, and Jin Jingfu, the manager of Tongyi, was elected as the deputy director. The total amount of reserve funds paid is 60,000 yuan. Anjiu Yu and the two Zhuang in Luxu each contributed 10,000 yuan. Xieji Zhuang, a member of the Luli, contributed 10,000 yuan, and Jinfeng, Tongyi, and Changfeng, the three members of Tongli, each contributed 10,000 yuan. The funds will be fully collected soon and officially established.

Wuxi Spring Cocoon Business Scheduled to Open 120

The Cocoon Industry Association of this county convened a general meeting of members at 2 pm on the previous day (30th), chaired by Hua Shaochun. First, the chairman reported on the issue of cocoon trade control. The association requested the authorities to consider and accommodate the three points: (1) Regarding the timing issue, the opening of the spring cocoon business this year is imminent, and there is not enough time for drawing lots, so we have to request a postponement. As for the construction of improved mechanical new stoves, we have to wait until next year. (2) Please do not collect improvement fees for the cocoon drying business. (3) The security deposit of 12 yuan per load is changed to 3 yuan per load. The association repeatedly argued for the above three requirements and asked the authorities to approve them. Then, discussions began, and it was resolved that (1) the cocoon trade house donation will still be collected by the association. (2) The stamp tax will be handled in accordance with the association's old plan. (3) The business tax was contracted by the association for 4,000 yuan last year, and this year, please ask the business tax bureau to collect it directly from the cocoon trade. (4) Cocoon trade houses that fail the grade and cocoon trade houses that have not been opened for two years and have less than four stoves that have a valid cocoon license should be opened as usual. As for the security deposit of 12 yuan, it is difficult to pay. The improvement fee of 3 yuan per load will be paid when the dry cocoons of each line are on the shelves, and the line license will be submitted to the county for review and registration first. The above points will be discussed again by the chairman with the authorities and reasonably negotiated. (5) The improved seed cocoon price is 25 yuan per load as the high price, and the local seed price is 20 yuan per load as the standard. (6) It was decided that the cocoon trade will open uniformly on June 4th. After the discussion, the meeting adjourned. Yesterday, more than 20 cocoon trade houses were reported to be opened, including Yu Changyong in Baishiqiao and Zhenxiangtai in Ge Diqiao. In addition, Zhang Guifang, the captain of the 9th Team of the 2nd District of the Water Police, went to the Cocoon Industry Association with Inspector Xiang Wengui yesterday to discuss the issue of protecting the cocoon market.

Incest and Abortion Lead to Death of Daughter-in-Law 121

In District 6, Map 18, Chen Douban Alley, resident Feng Chunquan, aged 45, has a son named Fogeng, aged 26. Since childhood, Fogeng was betrothed to Yin Apan, a woman from nearby Hexi. Yin came to live with them as a child bride at the age of six and is now 28, having already given birth to two sons and one daughter. Chunquan works as a temple keeper at the Zhang Xun Temple in Tangtou Township, while Fogeng used to collect tickets at the Paris Theater in the city. Yin, feeling lonely due to her husband's frequent absences, engaged in a clandestine affair with her father-in-law, Chunquan, resulting in incest. Recently, she became pregnant, being more than three months along. Fearing that her husband would find out, causing a loss of face, Yin hired a midwife to perform an abortion. However, after the procedure, she suddenly suffered excruciating abdominal pain and became bedridden. By the 28th of last month, her condition worsened, and she was immediately transported to the Brothers Hospital on the road for treatment. Unfortunately, her illness was too far advanced, and she passed away on the morning of the day before yesterday. The body was immediately transported back to her hometown, where the map leader, Shen Debiao, accompanied by the deceased's husband, Feng Fogeng, came to the local branch in the city, requesting an inspection. The acting prosecutor, at 9:00 AM yesterday, led officials to the countryside to conduct an autopsy. The autopsy revealed that the deceased, Feng Yin, had a hardened abdomen with the fetus still inside, confirming that she had died from excessive bleeding during the abortion, leading to extreme weakness. After the autopsy, the family was instructed to prepare for burial and await further investigation.
