Hao Gengsheng Discusses the Far Eastern Games 232

Hao Gengsheng, Physical Education Supervisor of the Ministry of Education, who attended the Far Eastern Games, returned to Nanjing on the 29th. According to him, the issue of winning or losing in the Far Eastern Games was a minor matter. The Japanese conspiracy (to have the puppet state join) and our country's efforts to respond were the major issues. Therefore, our country's representatives had a heavy responsibility. Our country's representatives and athletes were warmly welcomed by overseas Chinese in Hong Kong and the Philippines. In terms of competition results, apart from football and women's swimming, most were not as good. However, observing the efforts of each individual this time showed great progress compared to the past. For example, in baseball, our country usually pays little attention, and it was expected that we would be unable to compete. However, the result was only a narrow defeat of 4 to 1 and 4 to 0. In volleyball, we even managed to defeat the Philippines once. As for basketball, tennis, track and field, etc., although there were many failures, the score difference was not too great. From this, it can be seen that there has been significant progress in our country's physical education in recent years. Regarding the revision of the constitution, our representative argued rationally and firmly. The Japanese were unable to use their tricks. The Philippines, enticed by them, proposed that a special small committee be formed in addition to the general assembly, with representatives from China, Japan, and the Philippines as members. The general assembly would then transfer the revision of the constitution to this committee for discussion. Our side spoke eloquently, and the Japanese were unable to propose the puppet state in this committee. Our representative disagreed with the revision of the constitution and returned the case to the general assembly. The Japanese president wanted to open the general assembly early because he feared that this issue would affect this year's Games, so it was delayed until the 19th. During the general assembly, because the third article was not working, they tried to make tricks in the tenth article (group participation in the performance) and the fourteenth article of the supplementary rules, interpreting the so-called two-thirds. China took five units as the formal explanation. The Philippines was biased and wanted to vote for Japan. China considered it illegal and withdrew. The Japanese were unable to go any further and resorted to illegally dissolving the general assembly by enticing the Philippines. After the dissolution, the United States and the Philippines were in uproar, ignoring public opinion. The Philippines also felt uneasy. When our representatives and athletes returned home, the President of the Philippine Senate, Quezon (President of the Far Eastern Games from 1934 to 1935), had a conversation with our Dr. Wang Zhengting, saying that he would try his best to remedy the Far Eastern Games. Our country will consider how to proceed based on his approach. As for explaining the situation to the World Games, when China sent the athlete Liu Changchun to the World Games last time, the association did not recognize the puppet state, which was already a certainty. The illegal dissolution of the Far Eastern Games this time is enough to expose its shortcomings. Hao's thoughts on attending this time: (1) He felt that although the competition results were not as good as others in many respects, the people of all countries were able to do their best, which was much better than before. (2) Others have made more progress, and we have made less progress, so we can stimulate our determination to work hard for more progress in the future. (3) The Japanese are unreasonable, but their fighting spirit is commendable. For example, in football, which has always been very poor, although they lost this time, there were two matches where the score was 3 to 3 and 4 to 4 with us. Also, although volleyball is not good, they were able to defeat the Philippines once. From this, it can be seen that they have been working hard on weekdays, which our country can refer to. (4) There are many things to be done in domestic sports. We should be down-to-earth, strive for self-improvement, and work hard to fight so that we can show our true spirit in a suitable environment in the future. As for the Far Eastern Games, it is a place to show sports, but as long as we train, we can show something. The Far Eastern Games are another issue, and we should not stop eating because we are choked.

Ministry of Education Sports Committee Holds Meeting to Discuss Physical Education Testing Methods 236

The Ministry of Education's Sports Committee convened a meeting at the Ministry of Education at 5:00 PM on the 28th to discuss physical education testing matters with physical education teachers from public and private middle schools in the capital. Nineteen middle school physical education teachers attended. Chairman Zhang Jiong reported on the purpose of the meeting. Committee member Wu Yunrui reported on the testing methods that had been developed, saying that the former professor of Zhongda, McClay, had selected items that could be practiced universally and could represent physical education results at a glance, based on the physical education situation in Japan and the United States. There were no objections to the testing methods. All schools in Beijing were required to test according to these methods by the end of June, and the methods would be gradually promoted to Jiangsu, Shanghai, and other provinces and cities in the future. The testing methods are as follows:

Testing Methods 237

(1) How to Fill Out the Form

A. Age: It is best to fill in the actual age. If not, the old method of calculating age can be used, but it must be marked with the word "yin" after it.

B. It is best to have the Gregorian calendar birthday. Otherwise, the lunar calendar can be recorded, but it must be marked with the word "yin" after it.

C. Height is in inches.

D. Weight is in pounds.

(2) Management of Testing

A. 50-meter run: 50 meters for junior high school and below, and 50 meters for senior high school and above. When running, there must be one timer and one starter. When running 100 meters, two or three referees must be added. A stopwatch is sufficient for the 50-meter run because the distance is not long. If there is only one stopwatch for the 100-meter run, three or four people can run at the same time. The method is to first mark three or four lanes on the 100-meter track. At each lane, near the finish line, mark a horizontal line or make a mark every meter from the finish line to 75 meters. When running, the starter blows the whistle and simultaneously makes a downward waving motion with a towel. The timer presses the watch when they see the towel move. When they reach 11 seconds, they shout "Arrived!" or blow the whistle. A referee is assigned to each lane, standing on the side of the track inside the finish line, to be in charge of the distance reached by the runner in their lane. When they hear the timer blow the whistle or shout "Arrived!", they should pay attention to the distance reached by the runner, and then check the time from the following table.

12.1 seconds 100 meters 12.1 seconds 99.05 meters 15.1 seconds 76.39 meters

12.2 seconds 98.14 meters 15.2 seconds 75.79 meters

12.3 seconds 97.20 meters 15.3 seconds 75.20 meters

12.4 seconds 97.10 meters 15.4 seconds 74.61 meters

12.5 seconds 95.40 meters 15.5 seconds 74.03 meters

12.6 seconds 94.52 meters 15.6 seconds 73.46 meters

12.7 seconds 93.66 meters 15.7 seconds 72.90 meters

12.8 seconds 92.81 meters 15.8 seconds 72.34 meters

12.9 seconds 91.20 meters 15.9 seconds 71.79 meters

13.0 seconds 91.15 meters 16.0 seconds 71.79 meters

13.1 seconds 90.34 meters 16.1 seconds 70.76 meters

13.2 seconds 89.55 meters 16.2 seconds 70.18 meters

13.3 seconds 88.75 meters 16.3 seconds 69.66 meters

13.4 seconds 87.54 meters 16.4 seconds 69.15 meters

13.5 seconds 87.22 meters 16.5 seconds 68.6 meters

13.6 seconds 86.47 meters 16.6 seconds 68.13 meters

13.7 seconds 85.73 meters 16.7 seconds .63 meters

15.0 seconds 77.00 meters 18.0 seconds 61.67 meters

(2) Standing Long Jump (Senior High School Adds Running Long Jump)

Draw many lines on a mat or the ground, spaced one decimeter apart, from 1.5 meters to 2.5 meters. It is not necessary to measure the starting point when jumping. Each person takes three jumps in succession, and the longest distance is recorded.

(3) Running High Jump

This item is slow. If there are many people but only one high jump stand, each height is only allowed to be jumped once. If a height cannot be cleared, it can be raised again, but at most three attempts are allowed. However, the score is calculated based on the height that was cleared. When raising the height, senior high school students add 5 millimeters each time below 1 meter, and 3 millimeters above that. For junior high school students, add 5 millimeters each time below 8 centimeters, and 3 millimeters above that.

(4) Shot Put

8 pounds for junior high school, 12 pounds for senior high school, 6 pounds for women's junior high school, and 8 pounds for senior high school. If there is a shot put circle, use it. Otherwise, draw a lime circle with a diameter of 2.134 meters and use its center to draw several arcs of the same circle, spaced a quarter of a meter apart, from 4 meters to 12 meters. Each person takes three throws in succession, and the longest distance is recorded. To speed up the process of throwing, another circle can be set up opposite one circle, with the arcs overlapping each other.

(Note) All the above results should be transcribed onto the form. Please ask the Ministry of Education to purchase a scale for each school to use in rotation.

Spring and Autumn

Records of the Incense-Enshrouded Boudoir 252

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

Statement Regarding This Book

After its major revamp in early April, Spring and Autumn added the novel "Records of the Incense-Enshrouded Boudoir," translated by me. At that time, we had already stated in advance that our intention in publishing this novel was not to verify events of the previous dynasty, but simply to provide some variety for readers' interest. Later, in a preface written for this publication by Princess Rong Ling, the sister of the author Der Ling, and in my "Introduction to the Original Author," it was repeatedly stated that the content of this book is not entirely historical fact. Readers should only appreciate its exquisite embellishments and vivid writing, and not regard it as an accurate account of events in the Qing court. Because we know that novels are absolutely different from history, romances, and biographies; they contain many castles in the air fabricated by the author to connect the events in the book and please readers. Of course, this is not unique to "Records of the Incense-Enshrouded Boudoir"!

Recently, some people have made quite detailed corrections to the content of this book; from the standpoint of verifying events of the previous dynasty, this attitude is correct. However, since this is a novel, a different perspective should be adopted.

Spring and Autumn published this novel for three reasons:

(1) Der Ling previously wrote a book titled "Two Years in the Forbidden City," which was translated into Chinese and well-received by readers. She can be considered a pioneering female writer in China. In a China where female writers are still rare, we feel that we should introduce her works as much as possible.

(2) Although there are many exaggerated descriptions in the text, it is still quite interesting, and it portrays the personality of Empress Dowager Cixi very thoroughly, so it is still a good novel.

(3) Although the book is divided into thirty-five sections, each section can be separated, equivalent to twenty-five short stories; this structure is more suitable for our daily newspaper.

In order to increase readers' interest, after the entire book has been published, we will invite Princess Rong Ling and Mr. Xun Ling to write a detailed article verifying events of the Qing court, as if doing an accounting. If readers have any doubts now, they may wish to write them down one by one, and then compare them item by item with this verification, which would be even more interesting, wouldn't it?

Improved Silkworm Seed 253

— Yang Yusheng

It is said that due to the complete bankruptcy of the rural economy, many silkworm farmers are unable to purchase improved silkworm seeds at the very beginning of the silkworm season. Although they are well aware that the result of using "native seeds" year after year is a waste of effort, because native seeds do not require money to buy, even the small cost of silkworm seeds must be carefully calculated in these times of extreme economic hardship. They are truly pitifully poor! It is said that the silkworms that emerge from native seeds are mostly gluttonous and lazy. During the three molting periods, the amount of mulberry leaves "consumed" is substantial. Some turn black and decompose into a pile of foul-smelling liquid just after the third molt. This is certainly partly due to the influence of the weather, but the inherent unsoundness of the silkworm seeds and their lack of resistance are undeniable. Some show good signs during the third molt, but seem unwilling to "spin a cocoon" when they reach the spinning stage, holding their heads up and appearing unhappy. Silkworm farmers are truly both angry and anxious when they encounter these gluttonous and lazy creatures, and mostly throw them on the ground, where a flock of hens devours them piecemeal!

Improved seeds are not like that. They have undergone a series of forging procedures. Gluttonous and lazy silkworm seeds cannot withstand this forging, so they are all eliminated, and therefore cannot come out to harm people! Since improved seeds can withstand a series of forging procedures, the silkworm seeds themselves are naturally sounder. They have the ability to resist the "deterioration" and "decay" brought about by the weather, and can withstand "storms," so their contribution to humanity is particularly great. Although they may sometimes suffer from irresistible disasters, causing worry to silkworm farmers, the signs of premature death and gluttonous laziness that are typical of "native seeds" are rarely seen. Therefore, the market price of silk cocoons made from improved seeds is much higher than that of "native seeds." The latter, even if they escape the greedy mouths of chickens, are mostly thrown into the "ash pond" and turned into fertilizer. This is one way to make use of waste!

The Future of Stone Lake 254

— Yanqiao

My home, Stone Lake, in Suzhou, can be considered a good place. Its charm lies in its proximity to the city. Even the frailest, slowest-moving painted boat can reach the Xingchun Bridge in less than an hour. Especially along the Hengtang, there are green mountains and clear waters, more naturally beautiful than the Qili Shantang.

The Xingchun Bridge connects to the Nine-Ring Cave Bridge, like a curtain to Stone Lake. Lifting the curtain, the mirror-like lake, the gentle breeze, the entire Stone Lake is presented before you. In the middle is a small islet called the site of the Lakeside Pavilion, surrounded by reeds, reminiscent of Ruan Gong Pier in West Lake. To the left is the Yulang Village managed by the painter Wu Zishen, with its black walls and white corridors, and to the right are the remnants of the Haichao Temple, with its yellow walls and green grass, the colors harmonizing in a simple and pleasing way. Climbing to the Hushantang of Zhiping Temple, drinking a cup of tea, walking into the dense Shaolin, listening to the spring, admiring the solitary pagoda of Shangfang Mountain, and enjoying the scenery for a moment, I feel that this environment, where one can easily enjoy the pleasures of ascent and the delights of the heart and ears, is a pity to be shrouded in an atmosphere of superstition. If a road were built, ______, ______, and small houses were built, some red peach trees and green willows were planted, and a few small boats were allowed to float on the lake, wouldn't it be a wonderful Stone Lake Park? It seems that when Wang Yincai was the mayor of Suzhou, he had mentioned this idea, but the people of Suzhou are not enthusiastic about anything, especially beautifying the lake and mountains, considering it not urgent. In fact, the people of Suzhou have never worked hard on urgent matters either.

Mr. Li Yinquan often visited the mountains, forests, temples, and monasteries in this area, so he left many inscriptions. There are many stones in Zhiping Temple, all inscribed with words, which can be said to be the work of enthusiasts. According to the guide, many people come from all directions to offer incense after the Mid-Autumn Festival in August, and the people at the foot of the mountain rely on this to get a little benefit. Unfortunately, the monks on this mountain do not have the skillful methods of the Hangzhou monks, otherwise, how difficult would it be to start large-scale construction and decorate the mountains and forests in a new and attractive way?

Miscellaneous 255

— Yan Chonglou

People should be able to integrate with the group, and also be able to stand on their own away from the group.

When survival cannot be answered, life will feel exhausted.

People grow up in a vast world, but live in a very small world. Money from all directions flows to the city. The city's diseases flow to all directions.

Because they have not been hit, they dare to take great risks; once they encounter some setbacks, even a small amount of courage disappears!

People can sometimes solve a major problem in a very short time, but sometimes cannot solve a minor problem in a very long time.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 256

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Nine

Returning the Letter, Heartbroken and Self-Isolating

Swearing Brotherhood, Together Vowing Loyalty

Bao Fang nodded without adding any criticism. Just as they were talking, a rumbling sound suddenly approached. Looking up, they saw two enemy planes circling overhead. Whether their intention was to target the Ping'an village fortress was difficult to say. However, since the enemy planes were overhead, people should avoid being targeted, so Bao Fang gestured to Ziqiang, and everyone took shelter inside the house. After a long while, there was no movement, and the rumbling sound had faded away. When Ziqiang came out, he saw that Yin Deren was already outside. He smiled faintly, shrugging his shoulders. Although he did not speak, he seemed to be saying, "What's the big deal?" At the same time, he saw that he was holding many red and green leaflets and was looking around, as if he intended to find a few more. Ziqiang asked, "Did they drop these from the plane? What do they say on them? Let me see." Yin Deren laughed and said, "Is there any need to look? Even a cook could guess what they say. Looking at this will only cause panic. Let's not lead the brothers down this road." As he spoke, he rolled the leaflets into a bundle, pressed them on the ground, struck a match, and lit the leaflets. Before long, they had turned into a puff of blue smoke. Ziqiang laughed and said, "Second Brother, you are so clever and capable. I am not as good as you in everything." Yin Deren laughed and said, "I understand why you admire me. It's because you feel that I, as a bachelor, am too comfortable after you got married." Ziqiang sighed and said, "Comfortable or not, that's how it is for soldiers. But the mental pain I suffer is simply indescribable. This is something that you bachelors don't experience." Yin Deren said, "Hey! You're still thinking about your family. How can you lead your company of brothers like this?" (397)

Chatter

Cat Talk 257

— Zhu Yun

Besides "horse, cow, sheep, chicken, dog, pig," the cat is indeed an important animal among domestic animals: In Jiangnan families, almost every household keeps a cat. Cats not only catch mice, preventing those jumping clowns from stealing food and destroying things under the cover of darkness, disturbing residents, but also their gentle nature and pleasing fur are quite endearing. In the past, seven or eight out of ten young ladies in their boudoirs loved cats. I remember seeing a calendar with a painting of a beautiful woman by Zhang Mantuo, with a corner of the boudoir showing a fashionable woman teasing a kitten with a velvet rope in front of a roaring fireplace: the quiet scene could not help but evoke a feeling of lingering infatuation! Now, the times are gradually changing, and the temperament of young ladies is also changing with the wheels of time, from quiet to more active. In the arms or at the feet of modern ladies is a fluffy, foreign-bred puppy. However, the cat is still a lovely animal, with smooth fur that is so soft and adorable. The cat's character is somewhat like a tiger: its head must be round, its chin must be broad, its whole body must have powerful fur, and especially its tail, which can often stand upright, is a sign of a good mouse-catching cat. If the chin is narrow and the cat's mouth is pointed, it is sure to be a lazy cat. If the tail is often tucked between the buttocks, it is either sick or a cold and weak cat. Autumn cats are not good cats.

Among cats, those born in the spring are the best: at that time, silkworm cocoons are just hatching, so they are called "early silkworm cats." Because those cats mate in winter and go through wind and snow, they are physically strong, cold-resistant, and able to endure hardship. As for those cats born in summer or autumn, they spend their days in the stove during winter, requiring a blazing fire to be added to the stove door to emulate Cao Aman breaking through the encirclement at Chibi, sleeping all day in the rice straw ashes, unwilling to stick their heads out.

The appearance of cats can be roughly divided into two types: one is the lion cat, which is very cute because its fine fur is fluffy and resembles a lion. However, since the hair is fluffy and disheveled, it is naturally easy to accumulate dirt and grime. People who keep them must be diligent, loving, and attentive to grooming in order to keep them beautiful and clean. The other type is the ordinary cat. These cats can be further divided into several names based on the color of their fur. A cat with a completely black back and snow-white belly is called "black cloud covering snow"; a cat with a completely white body and a black tail is called "dragging a gun in the snow." There is also "iron rod hitting cherries," which refers to a cat with a yellow or black round spot on its forehead. The most common are tortoiseshell and tabby cats.

Female cats are more valuable than male cats, because female cats are only unwilling to settle down for a few days a year during their heat season. They usually maintain chastity and stay quietly at home, unlike male cats, which are sexually active all year round, pursuing mates, urinating along the way, and causing trouble, even neglecting their proper work of catching mice! Therefore, as the saying goes, "Female dogs and male cats, don't give them away to others." It is indeed something that is not welcomed by people, and cats and dogs are a clear example!

Cats' eyes can see in the dark, so they can catch mice in the dark. Those two eyes look like two green stars in the darkness. Some cats have eyes that look red and green in the dark, like gold and silver stars, which is called "gold and silver eyes" and are very capable of catching mice. Cats' pupils are the most peculiar, changing with the time of day; at midnight and noon, they look like a silver thread, then gradually become round, changing from a line to a shuttle, and from a shuttle to a perfect circle, as if it were a natural clock. Among treasures, there is a type called "cat's eye," which is said to be able to indicate time and is a priceless treasure.

Cats are carnivorous animals that catch mice, so fish is the main ingredient in their food. The time for cats to eat is generally around noon, because they need to catch mice at night. If they are fed too much, they will not be willing to catch mice. Therefore, there is a saying, "Feed the cat in the morning, feed the dog at night." Cats can live for about five or six to seven or eight years. One week after kittens are born, they can be fed sugar rice, and after half a month, they can eat ordinary rice. When kittens first start eating, adding some fried dough sticks (also known as fried rice cakes, a type of fried pasta) can prevent kittens from getting sick; in this era when veterinary medicine has not yet been fully developed, the only medicine for cats when they are sick is to buy some Wuyao, grind the juice, and feed it to them, which is considered the only way to treat cat illnesses.

GRAINS: NEGLIGIBLE VOLUME OF POWDER FUTURES DELIVERY 269

Yesterday was the delivery date for flour futures, but the market for futures was weak, and the delivery of spot flour was also minimal. KE-XIAN AND MIN-HUA RICE BECOME POPULAR AGAIN 270

Yesterday, the Ke-Xian rice market, after being popular for days, had already entered a stable trend. The amount arriving yesterday was not much, and the purchasing by merchants from Fujian province was active again, so the market seemed to have returned to a stable position. More than 5,000 bags were traded throughout the day, with 3,800 bags purchased by Fuzhou merchants, 800 bags by Quanzhou merchants, and 200-300 bags each by merchants from this street and Zhejiang province. The market prices were similar to the previous market, but the underlying trend was slightly firm. If not much more arrives in the future, the Ke-Hua market will easily change again.

NANJING NEW RAPESEED APPEARS ON THE MARKET 271

Yesterday, the first batch of 106 bags of new rapeseed from Nanjing arrived, with a price of 4 yuan. Today the weather is sunny, and the quality of later products will inevitably be better. It is hoped that the production area will improve the screening and cleaning. The market price in Beijing can be sold higher by a few yuan. Except for the Hankou cart soybeans, which rose by 4-5 cents due to the scarcity of goods ("previous day's opening price was 2.78 yuan"), the rest were firm and stable. High-grade Zhengyangguan soybeans were around 3 yuan, and medium-quality goods fluctuated by 2-3 cents. Yesterday, the market was slightly softened by the telegram drop, but fortunately, the factory demand was still continuous, and the amount arriving was scarce, so the market was tight.

SUGAR MARKET: TI-ZHUANG QING SUGAR OPENS UP BY FOUR CENTS 272

Yesterday, the sugar market remained relatively flat due to the firmness of Customs Gold Units. The guild's indicative price for No. 24 crude sugar white spot goods was 26 yuan, with few sellers. NORTH-SOUTH GOODS: GOLDEN MOUNTAIN BRANCHES PLUMMET, THEN PARTIALLY RECOVER 273

Since the price of Golden Mountain branches fell, the degree of decline has exceeded half of the original price. The reason for the sharp drop is that there are hopes for a bumper harvest of this year's new branches. Who knew that the market situation would suddenly change? According to letters from the production area, the recent lychees have suffered from insect pests and have been damaged by wind and rain, resulting in significant losses. Therefore, the market here has rebounded. It is said that the quoted price has risen by two to three yuan, but the trading price is still chaotic and has not yet risen excessively.

MID-GRADE RED DATES SOLD OUT IMMEDIATELY UPON ARRIVAL 274

Mid-grade red dates have been selling briskly recently, and the inventory is extremely scarce. For example, Haozhou red dates are already out of stock. It is said that several hundred bags will arrive in the next batch, and prices are bound to rise. The source of Fu red dates is not much. Because the Wenzhou and Taizhou merchants have a strong appetite, they are sold out as soon as they arrive, and the price has risen to 7 yuan.

SILK AND TEA: LOW PRICES FOR NEW SILKWORM COCOONS IN JIANGSU AND ZHEJIANG 275

(Shaoxing New Cocoons Arrive, Prices are Slightly Strong) The Shaoxing cocoon markets have been open for many days, and late silkworm cocoons have been listed. Late cocoons are mostly improved varieties with better quality. The market arrivals are gradually becoming active, but the cocoon markets are suppressing prices because they see that overseas silk prices have fallen again. Improved cocoons are only 25 to 30 yuan, and native cocoons are 15 to 25 yuan. Silkworm farmers have heavy leaf costs and are suffering losses. (Xiaoshan Cocoon Harvest Varies) The Xiaoshan silkworm harvest varies from village to village. Improved cocoons in the model areas of the eastern village are more abundant and of better quality. In the northwestern village, the native silkworms have run away seriously, with only 30-40% harvest, and the cocoons are of inferior quality. Only 23 cocoon markets in the whole county have opened, and they have been weighing cocoons for 4-5 days. The cocoon price is not high. The highest price for improved quality cocoons is only 35 yuan, and the highest price for native cocoons is 25 yuan.

(Haining Silkworm Farmers Reel Native Silk Themselves) Haining is a famous silk area, and new cocoons have been on the market for many days. Cocoon markets are offering low prices. Improved cocoons are only 30 yuan, and native cocoons are 20 yuan. Silkworm farmers are losing a lot of money, and many are reeling native silk themselves. Cocoon markets have only received tens to more than a hundred dan in a few days.

(Jintan Builds New-Style Cocoon Markets) Jintan County is a model silkworm area, and this year's silkworm harvest is expected to be bountiful again. The Jintan County Government has been ordered to build four new-style cocoon markets in the eastern village of Shuibei Town, the southern village of Shetou Town, the western village of Dongdalin, and the northern village of Zhongtang Town. They have jointly invested with major silk cocoon merchants in Wuxi to purchase four cocoon drying machines in Shanghai, worth more than 75,000 yuan, and have already transported them to various markets for installation. It is said that cocoon markets using machine-dried cocoons (using diesel) are being used for the first time in our country.

(New Style Cocoons from Chang'an Have Been Shipped to Shanghai) The new cocoons from Hangshao area of Zhejiang have been listed earliest. The fresh cocoons collected by the cocoon markets in Chang'an and other places have been baked into dry cocoons and delivered to the Huitong Transportation Company for shipment to Shanghai. There are dozens of packages of sample cocoons (both improved and native varieties) for testing. It is said that the shrinkage of fresh cocoons after baking is not great, averaging only 90 catties of dry cocoons for every 100 catties of fresh cocoons.

OIL MARKET: WHITE TUNG OIL GRADUALLY RISES 276

Foreign firms in Hankou continue to purchase white tung oil. After rising from 28 yuan to 29 yuan last week, oil merchants declared that they would not sell unless the price was 29.34 yuan. This week, foreign firms bought 200-300 tons at 29.4 yuan. Then, Hankou merchants wanted to sell at 29.8 yuan. Last night, it was reported from Hankou that foreign firms had purchased at 30 yuan, which shows that foreign firms' need for goods has been completely exposed. Therefore, the prices of goods from Hankou have also risen in tandem. Local tung oil has increased from 24 yuan to 25 yuan, and South Branch oil with taxes has also risen to 24.78 yuan. It is undeniable that the market is continuing to rise. However, now that foreign firms have reached 30 yuan, I don't think there will be any more surprises. Although the situation is different this year from previous years, it is still early in the season. Even if the production in the producing areas is lacking, the inventory will not be too thin. Although the source is scarce, there is no need to worry about interruption of supply. Even if foreign firms need goods urgently, there should be enough goods to supply. Therefore, even if it rises to more than 30 yuan, I am afraid it will be limited. However, after the rise, it is not easy to expect a return to relaxation. Although there may be small ups and downs, a big drop is hopeless. Therefore, everyone knows that the tung oil market this year has become a situation where it is easy to rise and difficult to fall. Hangzhou tung oil has been following the advances and retreats of the Hankou market. In the past two days, Hangzhou merchants wanted to sell at 20 yuan per stone, delivered in this port. However, merchants in this port did not want to chase the trend because they saw that domestic sales were not strong and the inventory was still available. Therefore, there were very few transactions. However, seeing that the Hankou market has risen again, they may be interested. But since another rise is feared to be limited, they are hesitating cautiously.

THE REASONS FOR THE SUDDEN RISE IN TUNG OIL 277

Tung oil, which has been in a slump, has suddenly turned higher. From spring to summer, there has been hardly a day when it has not been falling. Hankou Jing oil closed last winter at around 20 yuan per dan. After the beginning of spring, it went downhill day by day. At the beginning of last week, it was only selling for around 13 yuan. The lowest price for Macheng oil was 12.23 yuan. Who would have thought that people still expected it to be cheaper? All the markets were considered to have no possibility of turning around. Who knew that the inventories everywhere were already fixed, and there were many people who wanted to buy. Therefore, as soon as there was a start, everyone raised their prices together. According to the Hankou market, 4,000-5,000 pieces of Macheng oil have been sold since last week, with prices ranging from 12.34 yuan to 14 yuan. Heavy Jing oil rose from 13.23 yuan to 14.56 yuan. In total, there were over 10,000 pieces sold from the five categories of Jing, Zhi, Jin, Cha, and Ma. The buyers were from Shanghai, Ningbo, Suzhou, and Zhenjiang. The more it falls, the less people pay attention to it. As soon as there is a start, everyone will rush to buy. However, since the market has risen, buyers are also gradually constrained. Therefore, the current rising wind has seen a slight decline, and it can probably stand firm for a while.

Page 21

Free Talk

"Diary of the Wei Shui Xuan" 278

— Shu

One

I have three different editions of Li Rihua's diary in my collection. The first one I bought was the abridged version of "Xiao Juan Congshu" by Li Hanzhi (Li Rihua's great-grandson). It has a preface by the master of the Pianshi studio, Li Zhaoheng (Li Rihua's son), and Li Hanzhi, as well as a postscript by Zhuan Xiong, Ge Yuanxu. Later, I bought the complete edition engraved and printed by Jiayetang of the Liu family in Wuxing. In addition to Li Zhaoheng's preface, it also has postscripts by Wanwen Jushi and Liu Chengan. Liu's postscript describes the process of obtaining this manuscript in detail. The abridged version contains 155 entries, which is about two-eighths of the entire book. Last year, I also saw the Ming dynasty "Li Zhu Lan, Mr. Commentary", which includes three diaries: "Xi Zhao Lu," "Li Bai Yue Ji," and "Ji Xuan Lu." Among them, "Li Bai Yue Ji" was extracted from the complete manuscript, being the complete manuscript from April 5th to May 29th of the forty-second year of Wanli. "Xi Zhao" and "Ji Xuan" were written in the fifth year of Tianqi and after the complete manuscript of Jiayetang, but they do not have any particular advantages. The content of the diary, "starting from Yiyou in Wanli to Bingchen, divided by years. It records the review of poems and essays, the appraisal of calligraphy and paintings, and incidentally involves mountains, rivers, objects, plants, and tea" (master of the Pianshi studio). The language is concise and rhythmic. In the diary literature, it is a good book.

Two

When reading the diaries of ancient people, the most important thing is of course to understand the author's life. "From the late years of Emperor Shenzong of the Ming Dynasty, court officials formed factions and attacked each other. Rihua alone kept himself clean and retired, devoting himself to reading. Outside the dust and filth, he seemed to have found contentment" (Liu's postscript). Therefore, the life reflected in his diary is particularly characterized by a recluse style. He liked to travel in mountains and rivers, such as "On the eleventh day, He Xiaoyan and Yue Ji had a boat trip to invite me, mooring at the Rain Mist Pavilion. At that time, fragments of ice on the river touched the boat, and the setting sun shone on them like碎玉. Thousands of willows on the shore, with cold branches piercing the sky, travelers were nowhere to be seen. I thought it was clear, empty, and bright, surpassing this time, and surpassing the spring river moon night." Both his trips to Baiyue and Qiyun fully show his interests. He liked to grow flowers, and the diary mentions this aspect, such as "Whenever I am tired of reading, I walk among the flowers with a cane, winding and turning, which is very interesting. From then on, the shade of the trees, the color of the bamboo, the songs of the birds, and the fragrance of the flowers seem to be particularly abundant." Like "I drank a little wine with Shen Qian, Dai Shengheng, and my son under the flowers. At that time, seven or eight trees of red peach trees were like sitting in a cloud curtain, and two cranes danced with snowy feathers reflecting in between. The scenery was excellent, and Shen Qian's thoughts advanced rapidly, making it full of imagination." Gardens and mountains and rivers were Li Rihua's highest life interest. Therefore, in addition to visiting mountains and rivers and appreciating flowers, he also used a lot of effort to arrange his garden. He bought a pebble for more than 50,000 yuan to pave the ground, and bought 40 stones, "the large ones like crouching lions, and the small ones like lying foxes" to decorate the "mountain forest atmosphere," not afraid of the labor of "measuring the ropes and ink with the craftsmen, and the plasterers comparing the heights and lows, the fullness and narrowness." He was also particularly particular about food and drink. For example, drinking water: "The water carrier from Huishan returned, and I got more than 20 urns of new spring water. Five days ago, Zhaodu Yunshan's old monk sent me a bottle of pre-Qingming new buds. I opened it for a test, and the color, fragrance, and taste were all excellent." For example, food: "Shen Qian and Boyuan sent 40 yellow sparrows, fat, white, fresh, and crisp. I got the earliest taste of them. I drank at night and poured two cans." In his diary, we can simply organize a list of his favorite food and drink. Shen Zhou once said to Li Rihua: "I am about to burn all the books of Lu here, close the door and plant bamboo, so that the business will continue without interruption, and spread the unofficial history and miscellaneous sayings underneath, indulging in wine, laughter, and song." Li Rihua's personal life was actually like this: a retired aristocrat, a wealthy literati, relying on his wealth and the special skills of poetry and painting, escaped the "noise of the world" and lived a happy life.

Three

Regarding academic records in "Diary of Wei Bing Xuan", the main ones are on painting, as well as copying painting inscriptions, poems, and lyrics, which account for about two-halves of the entire book. For example, "On the twenty-second day, I went with Wan Xiang to view the large Chrysanthemum Irrigation painting by Lu Shuping of the countryside. The mountain ridges are steep, and the trees are sparse. Generally, the style of Zihou is used. The thatched cottage is located on a flat hill, surrounded by thin fences, and the trees are arranged in rows. Across the water, there is a pavilion, which is empty and can be seen. Two boys carry water and irrigate, one boy scoops water from the stream and pours it into the container, and two old men sit in front of the hall, one stroking the qin and the other hugging his knees, extremely spiritual. At the foot of the distant peaks of the back mountain, a pavilion stands tall, with a stone and fence foot. Small five-colored dots are used to gather into cold buds, shaking like the setting sun reflecting its light, and the light breeze brushing its posture. It is signed, 'Made by Lu Zhi of Baoshan on the ninth day of the ninth month of Renshen in the Canying Pavilion'". This type of writing about paintings is what Li Rihua is best at: detailed, concise, and extremely vivid. In addition, it is a book that deserves our attention in the diary. It introduces several leisure books and several masterpieces of essays. Although he is not entirely happy with leisure books, he has read "Jin Ping Mei" and his comment is: "Generally speaking, it is the most filthy thing in the market, and its sharpness is far less than "Water Margin". Yuan Zhonglang praised it extremely, but it is also an exaggeration of her strangeness". Not only did he express dissatisfaction with Zhonglang's praise of "Jin Ping Mei", he also did not agree with the literature of the Public Security School, like his teacher Chen Meigong. This can also be seen in the diary: "On the second day, it rained. I read the collection of Xu Wenchang. Yuan Zhonglang and Hongdao praised him as one of the contemporary people. However, his person is filthy and has strange qi, but he is not elegant. If it is poetry, it is vulgar and strange, very similar to Zhonglang, so there is a combination of stench. The zaju "Four Cries of the Ape" is a wonderful hand." He had read "Lamp Flower Granny" and "Laughing Record." His opinion on the "Laughing Record" was: "Although it is full of vulgar and mixed words from the market, after being provoked by it, it is extremely interesting, and a narrative is also humorous and pleasing," and he copied the original preface. In addition, he also talked about the three books "Xianyou", "Mengyou", and "Aoyou", citing the opinions of his friend Gu Zhu: "Recently published strange books, there are "Mengyou" and "Xianyou" two records, not words or legends, but 媪弹琵调也 while still have deep meanings. It is said that they were written by Yang Lianfu when he avoided the land in Jiangnan. There is also "Xiayou Lu" that has not been seen. Gu Zhu also said, "Our Ming Dynasty is behind the ancients in everything. What is outstanding is only tea, wine, ink, and the song of hitting dates", which is exactly the general view of the gentlemen at the time. There is one thing in the diary that is quite strange, that is, it says: Lu Fangweng also wrote a kind of "Shuchu Ji", and it is better than ("Shu Ru Ji"). But is it true or false? As far as I know, Fangweng has no such work.

ON THE MATTER OF QIN LIZHAI'S WIFE 279

— Gong Han

In recent years, articles about suicides due to economic oppression and moral constraints have been frequently seen in newspapers, but few people speak out or write about these. Only the suicide of Qin Lizhai's wife and her four children has caused quite a stir. Later, there was even a suicide victim who was carrying this news story, which shows its great influence. I think this is because there are many people. Single suicides are no longer enough to attract everyone's attention.

In all the echoes, although Qin's wife, the mastermind of the suicide, was treated with leniency, the conclusion was nothing more than condemnation. Because 丨丨commentators say丨丨although society is dark, the first responsibility of life is to survive. Suicide is a dereliction of duty. The second responsibility is to suffer. Suicide is seeking ease. Progressive commentators say that life is a battle. Suicide is desertion. Even death is not enough to cover up the crime. This can naturally be said, but it is too general.

There are criminologists who say that crime is due to the environment, and others say it is due to the individual. The latter saying is now popular, because if we believe the former, then eliminating criminals would require transforming the environment, which would be troublesome and scary. The critics of Qin's wife's suicide mostly belong to the latter.

Indeed, since she committed suicide, it proves that she is weak. But how did she become weak? It is important that we look at her father's letters, which scared her with the reputations of both families and moved her with the spirit's words of the deceased. We also have to look at her younger brother's eulogy: 'Wife died for her husband, children died for their mother...' Isn't there a great sense of regarding it as a beautiful story for the ages? How can a person who grows up and is nurtured in such a family not become weak? We certainly cannot start to blame for struggle, but the power of darkness to devour is often greater than that of a lone army. Moreover, the critics of suicide may not be supporters of struggle. When others are struggling, when they are struggling, when they are defeated, they may be silent. In remote rural areas or cities, how many orphans, widows, poor women, and laborers die obediently, or although they resist, they finally have to die? But who has ever spoken up or touched anyone's heart? It is truly 'they commit suicide in the ditches and no one knows it'!

People should of course survive, but for the sake of evolution. They may as well suffer, but for the sake of resolving all future suffering. They should fight even more, but for the sake of reform. Those who condemn the suicides of others should, while condemning others, also challenge and attack the environment that drives people to suicide.

Record of a Visit to a Friend in Wuxi 280

— Yuan

After Lady Lizhai and her daughter-in-law committed suicide together with medicine, I figured my old friend Pingfu must be experiencing extraordinary grief due to this family tragedy. I often considered ways to console him, but also feared further hurting the old man's feelings, so I hesitated to visit. Recently, a friend came from Wuxi and described Pingfu's recent condition, saying that his grief had lessened somewhat and he could勉强 see guests lately. The local authorities in the area were also concerned about the burial site for Mr. and Mrs. Lizhai, planning to use the funds originally allocated for Danruo School's expenses to subsidize the funeral, and wanted to discuss this with the old man. I accepted this mission and took the express train at 1 PM on the 26th, arriving in Wuxi at 4 PM. Upon arrival, I saw a sea of people outside the city, and when I asked, I learned that it was the Qingshan Temple Fair. and it would be followed by an all-night celebration, with people coming to watch from dozens of miles around. Asking about the reason for the temple fair, they said: (During the rampant Japanese pirate disturbances at the end of the Ming Dynasty, Wang Qiqin, the magistrate of Wuxi, concerned that the pirates would come to Wuxi to plunder, urgently supervised the workers to quickly build the city walls of Wuxi. As soon as the work was completed, the pirates arrived, and he led the local guard and civilians to defend against them. In the first battle, they were defeated, with thirty-six people killed. Subsequently, they gathered the people again and fought the pirates in the suburbs, defeating them greatly and preserving the entire city. Therefore, the local people admired him, and every year they held a fair to commemorate him. This year, because Japan's ambition to invade is increasingly rampant, the people of Wuxi's accumulated resentment is being vented through this fair, so it is particularly grand.) I usually dread commotion, and also feared road closures on my visit to my friend, so I went to bed early at No. 66 Wuxi Hotel.

The next morning at eight o'clock, I first went to Ronghu Villa Jiufeng Flour Mill to visit Mr. Cai Songru, only to learn that he had already gone to Shanghai yesterday. Our timing was off, which was very disappointing. Then I immediately went to Mr. Pingfu's outside residence at the foot of Lǐ City, and saw Pingfu's concubine. She said that Pingfu had gone out early to seek medicine because his young son was suffering from complications after the measles and was in great danger. (Pingfu's concubine has one son and one daughter, the son is nine years old and the daughter is eleven.) I was shocked and thought, how unlucky Pingfu is! So I immediately took my leave and went to the old residence in Xiaolou Lane to first meet Mr. Qin Xiaolu (Yuliu). Xiaolu is Pingfu's cousin and also an old friend of mine. Without exchanging pleasantries, I urgently asked about Pingfu's young nephew's illness, and Xiaolu said: "By the grace of Heaven, he is out of danger this morning. The past two days, the fever after the measles did not subside, and the Chinese medicine doctors were helpless. Yesterday, we changed to a Western doctor, and after taking the medicine, the fever subsided by evening and he is fine now." My heart was slightly relieved. Then I asked about Lady Lizhai's matter, whether the cause was exactly as the newspaper said? Xiaolu said: "Besides the two points mentioned in the newspaper, the deep affection between the couple and the discord with the mother-in-law, I absolutely do not know of any other reasons. Moreover, I had never heard of the so-called discord with the mother-in-law before. When Lizhai got married, she was still in school. The family was reunited, harmonious and peaceful. Everyone in our Qin clan envied Pingfu's family's happiness. Later, Lizhai went to Shanghai to work, and my niece-in-law Yin Xia also went to Shanghai. In recent years, every time I received news from Shanghai, they all said that Lizhai and his wife were virtuous, capable, and hardworking, able to support themselves, and often provided for the elders. Therefore, I initially did not know that there were disagreements between the mother-in-law and daughter-in-law. It was not until Yin Xia died and Pingfu's letter was published in the newspaper that I asked Pingfu about it. Pingfu said, 'On the surface, of course, the mother-in-law is kind and the daughter-in-law is filial, but in the hidden details, it is difficult for me to say.'" All I know is this. Xiaolu also said that my sister-in-law (Pingfu's wife) has recently returned to Wuxi from Shanhai, accompanied by her two daughters and two sons-in-law. The news of the deaths of Lizhai, Yin Xia, etc., was initially concealed from my sister-in-law. When she returned, they told her about Lizhai's death. My sister-in-law suddenly said: "If Lizhai died, my daughter-in-law Yin Xia must be dead!" I have always known their personalities; if the daughter-in-law dies, Lizhai will definitely die; if Lizhai dies, the daughter-in-law will not live alone. What exactly happened? Don't hide it from me!" Then they told her that Yin Xia had indeed died, and she stomped her feet and said: "Xiduan and Jue will also definitely die, the grandchildren's personalities are the same as their parents." Then they told her everything. At that time, my sister-in-law's grief and agitation, the tragic scene, I cannot bear to describe again. Fortunately, her daughters, sons-in-law, and family members tried their best to persuade and comfort her, and she is still under persuasion and prevention. I was very surprised at how deeply Pingfu's wife knew her son and daughter-in-law's personalities. At that time, Pingfu's two sons-in-law, one Gong and one Li, came out to see me, both gentle and capable. My friend, the old man, should be somewhat comforted, right? During the conversation, Pingfu arrived upon hearing the news, panting and hoarse, and we could hardly say a word to each other. Xiaolu explained my intentions on my behalf, and gradually touched upon the matter of Lady Lizhai's death. Pingfu said: "Alas! I initially had no intention of forcing my daughter-in-law to return to Wuxi. It was only because relatives all said: 'A widow and orphan, living alone in Shanghai, with no one to take care of them, how can I feel at ease?' I was also concerned about this, so I called them back. But who would have thought that it would come to this?" (I heard that in front of the spirits of Mr. and Mrs. Lizhai and their grandchildren, besides making two elegiac couplets to hang, there were also two plaques, one saying "Heaven, what sin have they committed?" and the other saying "Why did it come to this?" Both expressed the meaning of having grievances that could not be expressed). Having said this, he burst into tears. I dared not ask any further questions. Finally, I conveyed the intentions of the local authorities, asking if there was a burial site and whether the burial could be done this year? Xiaolu turned to Pingfu and said: "Strange, last night I dreamed that Lizhai, Yin Jin, and Xiduan Jue were sitting around a table, as if discussing something. Brother (referring to Pingfu) seemed to be among them as well. I was surprised that I did not know what they were discussing. Now that Mo Gong has come and mentioned this, could this be the matter?" Pingfu: "This must be settled quickly to put the dead at peace." He also said: "In our Qin family, according to past precedents, any children who die before the age of twenty cannot be buried in the order of generations. It seems that we cannot stick to the precedents this time, because Mr. and Mrs. Lizhai must want their children to live together in one place." Pingfu said: "Yes, there are no remaining burial plots in my ancestors' tombs. I myself must find another burial site. Together with Mr. and Mrs. Lizhai and their grandchildren, we must have a large plot of land for seven or eight coffins, so it will be difficult to find one at once." Xiaolu said: "The old tombs of the Qin family are all in Huishan, but now the prices in Huishan are expensive and there is no space to find. I think it is okay to go a little further, such as Yuantouzhu and other places, where prices are cheaper and easier to find. When I have some free time, I will help you find it." Pingfu said: "I must settle this matter this winter."

It was already noon. Xiaolu said: "Jinhua is returning to Wuxi today, and I have invited him to talk together. But the messenger returned and said that he had gone to Huishan." So we had lunch at Xiaolu's place. Those at the same table were me, Xiaolu, Pingfu, Xiaolu's son-in-law, and Pingfu's two sons-in-law. After the meal, Xiaolu said: "It is rare for you to come, and I have been living in seclusion for a long time. I was just thinking of going out for a tour. Pingfu is very depressed, please accompany us for a tour to relieve his mind, okay?" I dared not refuse, so we hired a car and first went to Mei Garden, sipping tea in the Songyan Hall and wandering for a long time. Then we went up to Taihu Hotel, leaning on the railing and looking out for a long time. The scenery was indeed very good, but none of us were in the mood for sightseeing today. And because it was already late, we did not go to Yuantouzhu, but turned back to Wuxi Hotel, sat and talked for a while. Pingfu and Xiaolu shook hands to say goodbye and left. I rested for a while in the apartment, and at 8:20, I went to the station to take the express train back to Shanghai. When I was about to leave, Mr. Jinhua sent a messenger to invite me to dinner, but because I was in a hurry to get on the train, I declined, feeling very apologetic.

In the train, I thought to myself: The Qin family is a harmonious and cheerful family. Yin Xia's parents-in-law are not comparable to the usual unreasonable people. There were no economic problems, but Yin Xia died like this! She led her children to die so calmly! Was her death, as some sympathizers say, commendable? Or, as critics say, was it unnecessary? This question lingered in my mind until the train wheels stopped, and my doubts were still unresolved.

The Living Puppet 281

Jumping the Ladder (4) 282

— Caoming

Similarly, A'mei went with an inquiring and trembling heart to accept this strong and crude man who spent all his labor in the fields during the day and snored loudly when he returned at night.

"Why are you afraid of me? Now, I am your husband." A'han said to A'mei with primitive crookedness and unaccustomed tenderness. However, she seemed even more clumsy in front of this strange and stubborn man. When her husband embraced her forcefully and warmly, she cried.

"Hey! You are not a child anymore, why are you crying? Ah, is there something that makes you uncomfortable?" the man lowered his head and asked in a low voice, holding his breath.

She raised her head, her moist and shimmering eyes staring at the man's face, her lips trembling with a smile she hadn't tried in ten years, and began to utter her clear voice:

"I know now, the world is still a little warm!"

After a short period, A'mei, like the rest of the women, lively carried the rice bucket to the fields. When she saw her husband, there were many words stored on the edge of her lips. The husband glanced at his wife who was reluctant to leave, but he held a cigarette and walked away.

The mother-in-law had eaten dinner, holding her water pipe and pacing out the door to find her conversational partner.

(It's like a plow cow, you can't say it has any disadvantages, but it only takes one step after being hit, it's very stupid!)

(That's right! But what about the next generation? How can such a stupid mother raise clever children? The next generation is important!)

Until the sun comfortably covers its face with gray-yellow silk, and fatigue invades the bodies of every worker.
